# Lyft Rental Program Terms

## Overview
- **Date**: 2026-06-15 04:30:19
- **Conversation ID**: `6a2fc629-a0f4-83ea-b1e8-8f574829eeb5`
- **Source**: `Chat-Export-28513-2026/conversations-009.json`

## Chat History

### User
> LYFT DRIVER RENTAL PROGRAM
> ADDENDUM TO RENTAL AGREEMENT TERMS AND CONDITIONS
> In connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program as provided in collaboration with Lyft, Inc. ("Lyft"), the following terms and conditions are hereby incorporated into the Rental Agreement Terms and Conditions (the "Agreement") between You and the Hertz company which is identified on the Rental Record ("Hertz"). Capitalized Terms used but not defined herein shall have the meanings assigned thereto in the Agreement. In the event of any conflict between the Agreement and the terms and conditions contained herein, these terms and conditions of this Addendum shall control.
> 
> Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, the only person authorized to operate the Car is You, and no Commercial Passengers (as defined below) are permitted within the Car except as contemplated by Item 2 below.
> Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, the use of the Car to carry persons "for hire" ("Commercial Passengers") is authorized only with respect to transportation of passengers via the Lyft application (and no applications or platforms provided by other transportation network companies) originating from locations within the "authorized territory" for Lyft operations as designated through the Lyft application, and for which the Lyft application remains on in driver mode until all passengers exit the Car. Any other “for hire” transportation is a violation of the Agreement and this Addendum.
> You represent, warrant and covenant to Hertz that You have all licenses, permits and approvals required to perform the "for hire" services contemplated by Item 2 above pursuant to, and that You will perform such services in accordance with, all applicable laws, regulations, permits, licenses, administrative pronouncements and court rulings, including without limitation those governing transportation network companies and drivers utilizing their platforms as well as those governing the provision of “for hire” transportation services at airports or other transportation hubs.
> You authorize Hertz to provide personal information about You and each rental You undertake using an identifying Lyft customer discount program (CDP) number or otherwise in connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program to Lyft for CDP eligibility, rental charge deduction, and other purposes. You also authorize the transfer by Hertz of Your personal information to the owner of the Car or any other third parties. Hertz makes no representations or warranties as to the use of such information by Lyft, the owner of the Car or any such third party, and by signing this Addendum, You expressly discharge any claims of responsibility of Hertz regarding the misuse of information by Lyft, the owner of the Car or any such third party. Such information may include, but is not limited to: name; birth date; contact information (phone number, e-mail address, mailing address, etc.); driver’s license number, state of issuance and expiration date; charges applicable to the rental; insurance information; Car usage information (including geolocation, speed, and other data); Car license plate issuing state and number; Car make, model, year, mileage, color and number of doors; rental location; background and financial information; and rental history (including current rental and due date). You further acknowledge and agree that Lyft may provide personal information about You to Hertz, including without limitation information about Your usage of the Lyft application and the amount of Your earnings on the Lyft platform and that Your usage of the Lyft platform is subject in all respects to Lyft’s terms of service.
> You acknowledge and agree that, to the extent permitted by law, Hertz may take disciplinary or other action on the basis of Your driving behavior and driving behavior data (including, but not limited to geolocation, speed, mileage, braking, and damage data) derived from in-vehicle telematics and other devices or gauges, which action may include suspension or termination of your ability to continue to participate in the Lyft Driver Rental Program or otherwise to rent vehicles from Hertz or its affiliates.
> You acknowledge and agree that Hertz may coordinate with Lyft to deduct any amounts You owe in connection with the rental from the amounts You may earn while providing for-hire transportation services on the Lyft platform, including without limitation all rental charges, fees or deductibles related to Car damage (including those described in Section 6 below), fines, tolls or any additional fees incurred in connection with Your rental from Hertz, and in addition that Lyft may require You to provide a credit or other payment card (subject to applicable terms and conditions) in order to reserve or rent a vehicle, that an authorization or hold amount may be placed on the card provided, and that Lyft may charge the amount owed to the payment card You provide at any time. Hertz has designated Lyft as its agent solely for the purpose of collecting these amounts on Hertz’s behalf. For this purpose, You authorize Lyft to offset these amounts from other amounts Lyft owes You, and if such offset does not fully pay such amounts, to charge the remaining unpaid amount to the payment method You have authorized for Lyft’s use in connection with the Lyft platform. Any such amounts shall be collected at least weekly during the rental period. Certain amounts may be charged at or after the end of the rental period, such as fees for Car damage as may be identified during final inspection, or for unpaid tickets or tolls and associated administrative fees that are identified after the rental period, or otherwise, as provided in the Agreement. You must keep a valid payment method on file with Lyft to pay the above amounts. If Lyft is collecting these amounts, You will receive a summary in Your weekly online statement from Lyft with the breakdown of amounts owed during, and as applicable after, the rental period. Estimated weekly rental charges will be assessed by Lyft on a pro-rata basis from Monday at 5:00am through the following Monday at 4:59am but would not reflect all amounts You may owe in connection with your rental. Amounts will be deducted from Your account or charged to the payment method You have authorized for Lyft’s use in connection with the Lyft platform each Tuesday for the prior weekly period. In addition or in the alternative, Hertz may elect to collect such amounts directly from You through mechanisms Hertz may make available to You from time to time (which mechanisms may require that you provide a credit or other payment card (subject to applicable terms and conditions) in order to reserve or rent a vehicle, that an authorization or hold amount may be placed on the card provided or a deposit may be charged on such payment card, and that Hertz may charge the amount owed to the payment card You provide at any time), and in the event the amounts remitted by Lyft to Hertz with respect to Your rental are not sufficient to satisfy amounts You owe to Hertz, Hertz may exercise any remedies available to collect such amounts directly from You.
> You hereby agree that, notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, a One Thousand Dollar ($1,000) deductible will apply to the Loss Damage Waiver (LDW), and the LDW will be included with Your rental solely for damage to the vehicle occurring while not using the Lyft application or when using the Lyft application in driver mode (available to receive ride requests) but not en route to pick up a passenger or driving a passenger up to and including passenger drop-off. As a result, You will be responsible for loss of and/or damage to the Car during such period of up One Thousand Dollars ($1,000). For the period of time when the Lyft application is in passenger mode (en route to pick up passenger, driving passenger and up to and including passenger drop-off), You will be responsible for any loss of and/or damage to the Car during such periods of up to One Thousand Dollars ($1,000), contingent on Your compliance with the terms and conditions of Lyft’s then-effective Terms of Service. LDW is contingent on Your compliance with the terms and conditions of the Agreement and this Addendum. For purposes of clarity, You may not be eligible for the purchase of Partial Damage Waiver (PDW) or Limited Loss Damage Waiver (LLDW) in connection with Your rental. You waive any claims related to the provision of Damage Waivers or limits thereto under state law. You are responsible for any third party liability in connection with your operation of the Car (but, assuming Your compliance with the Agreement, and this Addendum, only to the extent of such liability incurred in excess of the minimum financial responsibility limits of the applicable state). You should refer to Lyft’s terms and conditions for any collision or third party liability coverage they may provide. Terms and conditions apply to all protection and insurance products. Additional LDW terms can be found in the Agreement and online.
> Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, You may not be eligible to purchase any optional insurance products from Hertz in connection with Your rental, including without limitation Liability Insurance Supplement (LIS), Personal Accident Insurance (PAI) / personal effects coverage (PEC) or Emergency Sickness Protection (ESP).
> You acknowledge and agree that You may be responsible for the full amount of any liability arising in connection with the Car during the duration of Your rental and in accordance with the Agreement.
> You acknowledge and agree in the event of any accident, theft or other liability incident involving the Car during the rental period, You will provide Hertz a copy of the insurance policy covering Your use of the Car (if any) or which may respond to any automobile liability involving the Car.
> PLEASE NOTE: Some Lyft Driver Rental Program rental vehicles require diesel fuel. You must refuel your rental vehicle with the correct type of fuel for the vehicle, which will likely be noted in the owner’s manual or on the reverse of the gas cap. You are responsible for any damage that occurs to the vehicle as a result of improper refueling.
> Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in the Agreement or the Rental Record, in no event shall the term of any rental extend beyond the earlier of fifty-six (56) days after the first day of the rental (the “Combined Maximum Rental Period”) or the expiration or termination of the Lyft Driver Rental Program in the geographic region of the rental.
> Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in the Agreement or the Rental Record, You must return the Car at, or at Hertz’ discretion and upon notice to You from Hertz or Lyft prior to, the end of the weekly rental period if your rental is not renewed for another week, and in no event later than the Combined Maximum Rental Period, or in connection with any voluntary exchange of the Car, to the location from which it was rented during normal business hours for such location. If the Car is not returned at such time, Hertz will attempt to contact you using the information you have provided. If after attempted contact, the Car is not returned immediately, Hertz may report the Car as stolen. Any failure to return the Car as described above will be a breach of the Agreement and You will be subject, among other things, to additional charges, penalty fees and/or rate reversions.
> If, in connection with an exchange of the Car due to a mechanical issue, Hertz is unable to provide You with a Car eligible for participation in the Lyft Driver Rental Program, you may not use such replacement Car to perform the "for hire" services contemplated by Item 2 above, but may return such replacement Car to the location from which the original (replaced) Car was rented during normal business hours for such location in order to exchange the replacement Car with a Car eligible for participation in the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> You agree to indemnify, defend and hold Hertz and Lyft harmless from any and all losses, damages, liabilities, injuries, claims, demands, expenses and costs (including, without limitation, attorneys’ fees and expenses) which Hertz or Lyft may incur by reason of, or arising out of, Your (i) breach or violation of, or failure to observe or perform any term, provision or covenant of, the Agreement or this Addendum, or (ii) Your performance of services as a participating driver on the Lyft platform. This indemnification is in addition to, and not in lieu of, any indemnification by You set forth in the Agreement, and shall survive the termination of the Agreement.
> You acknowledge and agree that You are not permitted to perform any work or service whatsoever for Hertz under the terms of the Lyft Driver Rental Program and warrant and represent that You shall not do so. You further acknowledge and agree that while participating in the Lyft Driver Rental Program You are not nor shall You be construed in any way as an employee, contractor, or vendor of Hertz, that You shall not be entitled to any benefits accorded by Hertz to its employee, including without limitation workers compensation, disability insurance, vacation, or sick pay, and that the only relationship You have with Hertz is as defined under the terms of the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> You expressly agree that Lyft shall be a third party beneficiary of this Addendum for purposes of enforcing Sections 4, 5, 6, 13 and 15 hereof against You.
> You acknowledge and agree that, in the event You fail to satisfy the requirements provided by Lyft in connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program, and therefore do not qualify as a Qualified LRP Driver under the Lyft Rental Program with Hertz, You shall be charged the then-current market rate for the Car for the entire duration of the rental and will be required to return the Car. Those requirements include, without limitation:
> Complete at least twenty (20) rides on the Lyft Platform for each calendar week during the rental period.
> Comply with Lyft's terms of service and maintain good standing on the Lyft platform at all times during the rental period; and
> Comply with the terms of the Agreement as modified by this Addendum for such rental.
> You acknowledge and agree that in the event that your prior scheduled rental due date has passed, and you have kept your rental vehicle, the rental period will be automatically extended for an additional week, for a maximum of 7 weeks, provided that you have sufficient funds in Your account with Lyft and continue to be in compliance with the Agreement as modified by this Addendum. However, in the event you receive notice to return your rental vehicle for it being late, you must do so. You acknowledge that you have no right to extension of a rental and Hertz may refuse to extend Your rental or permit you to rent again (under this program or for any other purpose) for any reason, including without limitation excessive mileage or wear and tear on the Car. If a rental is not extended at the discretion of Hertz, regular late fees will apply.

### Assistant
> This addendum is **not great for you**, but it also gives you some useful leverage. The key is separating:
> 
> 1. **What Hertz/Lyft are allowed to charge under the program**
> 2. **What they actually disclosed/represented to you**
> 3. **Whether the vehicle/program failure made the rental unusable or unsafe**
> 4. **Whether optional add-ons were charged without valid consent**
> 
> ## The biggest clauses that matter
> 
> ### 1. Lyft-only commercial use
> 
> You can only use the rental for **Lyft rides**, not Uber, DoorDash, GoPuff, Roadie, etc.
> 
> That matters because if you were using or planning to use other platforms with that car, Hertz/Lyft could call that a violation. Do **not** put anything in your complaint that implies you were using the car for other gig platforms.
> 
> Keep the complaint framed around:
> 
> > I rented this vehicle specifically through the Lyft Driver Rental Program to perform Lyft rides.
> 
> ### 2. Charges can be deducted weekly
> 
> This clause gives Lyft/Hertz permission to deduct rental charges, damage fees, tolls, tickets, deductibles, and other rental amounts from Lyft earnings or your payment method.
> 
> So the fact that they charged weekly is probably allowed.
> 
> But that does **not** automatically mean every charge was valid.
> 
> Your stronger issue is:
> 
> > I was charged optional or add-on products that I did not knowingly authorize, and I was represented that certain protections/roadside services were already included in the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> 
> ### 3. LDW is included, but with a $1,000 deductible
> 
> This is important. The addendum says:
> 
> > “LDW will be included with Your rental…”
> 
> That supports your argument that **damage protection was part of the program**, not necessarily some optional upsell you knowingly purchased.
> 
> But watch the trap: the included LDW has a **$1,000 deductible**, and it applies differently depending on whether you are offline, online, or actively on a Lyft trip.
> 
> So your clean argument is **not** “I had full free coverage for everything.”
> 
> Your cleaner argument is:
> 
> > The rental program documents and addendum indicate LDW/damage protection was included. I did not knowingly agree to pay an additional weekly LDW add-on charge beyond the included program protection, and Hertz staff did not clearly disclose that I was purchasing a separate optional product.
> 
> ### 4. Optional insurance may not even be available
> 
> The addendum says you may not be eligible to purchase optional insurance products from Hertz, including LIS, PAI/PEC, ESP.
> 
> That helps you question what exactly they sold you.
> 
> If the receipt shows charges like:
> 
> - LDW
> - Premium Roadside
> - tax on LDW
> - roadside protection
> - optional coverage
> 
> Then you can ask:
> 
> > Please identify the exact product charged, whether it was optional or mandatory, where I signed for it, and how it differs from the LDW/roadside protections represented as included in the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> 
> That is a strong paper-trail demand.
> 
> ### 5. 20 rides per week required
> 
> The addendum says you must complete at least **20 Lyft rides per calendar week**. If you do not, they can charge the market rate and require return.
> 
> This matters because your complaint should emphasize that Hertz’s delay and defective/unsafe vehicle issues interfered with your ability to complete the required rides.
> 
> Say it like this:
> 
> > Hertz’s failure to timely resolve the plate/sticker and vehicle/key-fob issues materially interfered with my ability to use the vehicle for its intended Lyft rental purpose, including meeting program requirements.
> 
> ### 6. Mechanical exchange clause
> 
> This clause says if there is a mechanical issue and they give you a replacement car that is not Lyft-eligible, you cannot use that replacement for Lyft.
> 
> That means Hertz knew the program depends on providing a **Lyft-eligible, usable vehicle**.
> 
> Useful framing:
> 
> > The rental was not just transportation; it was a Lyft Driver Rental Program vehicle. A non-compliant, unusable, or unsafe vehicle defeats the entire purpose of the rental.
> 
> ### 7. Return / stolen vehicle language
> 
> This is the danger clause.
> 
> If they tell you to return it, and you do not, they can escalate and potentially report it stolen after attempted contact.
> 
> So do not play chicken with them. Keep everything documented. If you cannot return because of money/payment/program confusion, send written notice.
> 
> Your position should be:
> 
> > I am not refusing to return the vehicle. I am disputing unauthorized/invalid charges and requesting immediate correction, documentation, and a safe compliant resolution.
> 
> ## Your strongest complaint theory
> 
> The strongest version is **not** “Hertz charged me and that’s illegal.”
> 
> The stronger, cleaner version is:
> 
> > Hertz/Lyft represented this rental program as including damage protection, roadside assistance, maintenance, and Lyft-eligible use. I was charged additional LDW/roadside amounts that were not clearly authorized or properly disclosed. Then Hertz failed to timely correct a plate/sticker issue and key/battery issue, leaving me stranded and unable to safely or reliably use the vehicle for the Lyft Driver Rental Program. I am requesting refund/removal of unauthorized optional charges, correction of the account balance, and a safe Lyft-eligible replacement or documented return process without penalty caused by Hertz’s delay.
> 
> That’s the lane. Stay there.
> 
> ## What I would demand from Hertz/Lyft
> 
> Ask for these in writing:
> 
> 1. **Full itemized rental ledger**
>    Include base rate, taxes, LDW, roadside, fees, deposits, holds, payments, and Lyft deductions.
> 
> 2. **Signed proof of optional add-ons**
>    Ask for the exact document, timestamp, screen, initials, or signature where you agreed to additional LDW and Premium Roadside.
> 
> 3. **Explanation of included vs charged LDW**
>    Since the addendum says LDW is included, they need to explain why you were charged extra.
> 
> 4. **Refund/removal of unauthorized optional charges**
>    Especially LDW and Premium Roadside if they cannot prove valid authorization.
> 
> 5. **Credit/adjustment for unusable rental period**
>    Because the sticker/plate and vehicle/key/battery issue prevented normal use.
> 
> 6. **Written confirmation of current return/swap status**
>    You want protection against them later claiming you ignored instructions.
> 
> ## One line you should absolutely use
> 
> > Please explain how the separate LDW and Premium Roadside charges were authorized, given that the Lyft Driver Rental Program materials and addendum represent damage protection/LDW and roadside-related support as included in the rental program.
> 
> That’s the pressure point.
> 
> ## Watch your wording
> 
> Do **not** say:
> 
> > “I had full insurance included.”
> 
> Say:
> 
> > “The program represented LDW/damage protection as included, subject to the program deductible and terms.”
> 
> Do **not** say:
> 
> > “I could use the car for all gig work.”
> 
> Say:
> 
> > “The car was rented specifically for Lyft Driver Rental Program use.”
> 
> Do **not** say:
> 
> > “I refused to return it.”
> 
> Say:
> 
> > “I remained in communication and sought a safe, compliant resolution while disputing charges and vehicle usability issues.”
> 
> ## Bottom line
> 
> This addendum gives Hertz/Lyft broad power to collect weekly charges and enforce the program rules. But it also supports your argument that **LDW was included**, that the car needed to be **Lyft-eligible and usable**, and that Hertz’s failure to resolve the sticker/key/battery situation interfered with the entire purpose of the rental.
> 
> Your best fight is **unauthorized add-ons + unusable rental + unsafe delay**, not a broad “all charges are invalid” argument.

### User
> # LYFT DRIVER RENTAL PROGRAM
> # 
> # ADDENDUM TO RENTAL AGREEMENT TERMS AND CONDITIONS
> In connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program as provided in collaboration with Lyft, Inc. ("Lyft"), the following terms and conditions are hereby incorporated into the Rental Agreement Terms and Conditions (the "Agreement") between You and the Hertz company which is identified on the Rental Record ("Hertz"). Capitalized Terms used but not defined herein shall have the meanings assigned thereto in the Agreement. In the event of any conflict between the Agreement and the terms and conditions contained herein, these terms and conditions of this Addendum shall control.
> 1. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, the only person authorized to operate the Car is You, and no Commercial Passengers (as defined below) are permitted within the Car except as contemplated by Item 2 below.
> 2. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, the use of the Car to carry persons "for hire" ("Commercial Passengers") is authorized only with respect to transportation of passengers via the Lyft application (and no applications or platforms provided by other transportation network companies) originating from locations within the "authorized territory" for Lyft operations as designated through the Lyft application, and for which the Lyft application remains on in driver mode until all passengers exit the Car. Any other “for hire” transportation is a violation of the Agreement and this Addendum.
> 3. You represent, warrant and covenant to Hertz that You have all licenses, permits and approvals required to perform the "for hire" services contemplated by Item 2 above pursuant to, and that You will perform such services in accordance with, all applicable laws, regulations, permits, licenses, administrative pronouncements and court rulings, including without limitation those governing transportation network companies and drivers utilizing their platforms as well as those governing the provision of “for hire” transportation services at airports or other transportation hubs.
> 4. You authorize Hertz to provide personal information about You and each rental You undertake using an identifying Lyft customer discount program (CDP) number or otherwise in connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program to Lyft for CDP eligibility, rental charge deduction, and other purposes. You also authorize the transfer by Hertz of Your personal information to the owner of the Car or any other third parties. Hertz makes no representations or warranties as to the use of such information by Lyft, the owner of the Car or any such third party, and by signing this Addendum, You expressly discharge any claims of responsibility of Hertz regarding the misuse of information by Lyft, the owner of the Car or any such third party. Such information may include, but is not limited to: name; birth date; contact information (phone number, e-mail address, mailing address, etc.); driver’s license number, state of issuance and expiration date; charges applicable to the rental; insurance information; Car usage information (including geolocation, speed, and other data); Car license plate issuing state and number; Car make, model, year, mileage, color and number of doors; rental location; background and financial information; and rental history (including current rental and due date). You further acknowledge and agree that Lyft may provide personal information about You to Hertz, including without limitation information about Your usage of the Lyft application and the amount of Your earnings on the Lyft platform and that Your usage of the Lyft platform is subject in all respects to Lyft’s terms of service.
> 5. You acknowledge and agree that, to the extent permitted by law, Hertz may take disciplinary or other action on the basis of Your driving behavior and driving behavior data (including, but not limited to geolocation, speed, mileage, braking, and damage data) derived from in-vehicle telematics and other devices or gauges, which action may include suspension or termination of your ability to continue to participate in the Lyft Driver Rental Program or otherwise to rent vehicles from Hertz or its affiliates.
> 6. You acknowledge and agree that Hertz may coordinate with Lyft to deduct any amounts You owe in connection with the rental from the amounts You may earn while providing for-hire transportation services on the Lyft platform, including without limitation all rental charges, fees or deductibles related to Car damage (including those described in Section 6 below), fines, tolls or any additional fees incurred in connection with Your rental from Hertz, and in addition that Lyft may require You to provide a credit or other payment card (subject to applicable terms and conditions) in order to reserve or rent a vehicle, that an authorization or hold amount may be placed on the card provided, and that Lyft may charge the amount owed to the payment card You provide at any time. Hertz has designated Lyft as its agent solely for the purpose of collecting these amounts on Hertz’s behalf. For this purpose, You authorize Lyft to offset these amounts from other amounts Lyft owes You, and if such offset does not fully pay such amounts, to charge the remaining unpaid amount to the payment method You have authorized for Lyft’s use in connection with the Lyft platform. Any such amounts shall be collected at least weekly during the rental period. Certain amounts may be charged at or after the end of the rental period, such as fees for Car damage as may be identified during final inspection, or for unpaid tickets or tolls and associated administrative fees that are identified after the rental period, or otherwise, as provided in the Agreement. You must keep a valid payment method on file with Lyft to pay the above amounts. If Lyft is collecting these amounts, You will receive a summary in Your weekly online statement from Lyft with the breakdown of amounts owed during, and as applicable after, the rental period. Estimated weekly rental charges will be assessed by Lyft on a pro-rata basis from Monday at 5:00am through the following Monday at 4:59am but would not reflect all amounts You may owe in connection with your rental. Amounts will be deducted from Your account or charged to the payment method You have authorized for Lyft’s use in connection with the Lyft platform each Tuesday for the prior weekly period. In addition or in the alternative, Hertz may elect to collect such amounts directly from You through mechanisms Hertz may make available to You from time to time (which mechanisms may require that you provide a credit or other payment card (subject to applicable terms and conditions) in order to reserve or rent a vehicle, that an authorization or hold amount may be placed on the card provided or a deposit may be charged on such payment card, and that Hertz may charge the amount owed to the payment card You provide at any time), and in the event the amounts remitted by Lyft to Hertz with respect to Your rental are not sufficient to satisfy amounts You owe to Hertz, Hertz may exercise any remedies available to collect such amounts directly from You.
> 7. You hereby agree that, notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, a One Thousand Dollar ($1,000) deductible will apply to the Loss Damage Waiver (LDW), and the LDW will be included with Your rental solely for damage to the vehicle occurring while not using the Lyft application or when using the Lyft application in driver mode (available to receive ride requests) but not en route to pick up a passenger or driving a passenger up to and including passenger drop-off. As a result, You will be responsible for loss of and/or damage to the Car during such period of up One Thousand Dollars ($1,000). For the period of time when the Lyft application is in passenger mode (en route to pick up passenger, driving passenger and up to and including passenger drop-off), You will be responsible for any loss of and/or damage to the Car during such periods of up to One Thousand Dollars ($1,000), contingent on Your compliance with the terms and conditions of Lyft’s then-effective Terms of Service. LDW is contingent on Your compliance with the terms and conditions of the Agreement and this Addendum. For purposes of clarity, You may not be eligible for the purchase of Partial Damage Waiver (PDW) or Limited Loss Damage Waiver (LLDW) in connection with Your rental. You waive any claims related to the provision of Damage Waivers or limits thereto under state law. You are responsible for any third party liability in connection with your operation of the Car (but, assuming Your compliance with the Agreement, and this Addendum, only to the extent of such liability incurred in excess of the minimum financial responsibility limits of the applicable state). You should refer to Lyft’s terms and conditions for any collision or third party liability coverage they may provide. Terms and conditions apply to all protection and insurance products. Additional LDW terms can be found in the Agreement and online.
> 8. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary contained in the Agreement or any other agreement between You and Hertz or any of its affiliates, You may not be eligible to purchase any optional insurance products from Hertz in connection with Your rental, including without limitation Liability Insurance Supplement (LIS), Personal Accident Insurance (PAI) / personal effects coverage (PEC) or Emergency Sickness Protection (ESP).
> 9. You acknowledge and agree that You may be responsible for the full amount of any liability arising in connection with the Car during the duration of Your rental and in accordance with the Agreement.
> 10. You acknowledge and agree in the event of any accident, theft or other liability incident involving the Car during the rental period, You will provide Hertz a copy of the insurance policy covering Your use of the Car (if any) or which may respond to any automobile liability involving the Car.
> 11. **PLEASE NOTE:** Some Lyft Driver Rental Program rental vehicles require diesel fuel. **You must refuel your rental vehicle with the correct type of fuel for the vehicle**, which will likely be noted in the owner’s manual or on the reverse of the gas cap. You are responsible for any damage that occurs to the vehicle as a result of improper refueling.
> 12. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in the Agreement or the Rental Record, in no event shall the term of any rental extend beyond the earlier of fifty-six (56) days after the first day of the rental (the “Combined Maximum Rental Period”) or the expiration or termination of the Lyft Driver Rental Program in the geographic region of the rental.
> 13. Notwithstanding anything to the contrary in the Agreement or the Rental Record, You must return the Car at, or at Hertz’ discretion and upon notice to You from Hertz or Lyft prior to, the end of the weekly rental period if your rental is not renewed for another week, and in no event later than the Combined Maximum Rental Period, or in connection with any voluntary exchange of the Car, to the location from which it was rented during normal business hours for such location. If the Car is not returned at such time, Hertz will attempt to contact you using the information you have provided. If after attempted contact, the Car is not returned immediately, Hertz may report the Car as stolen. Any failure to return the Car as described above will be a breach of the Agreement and You will be subject, among other things, to additional charges, penalty fees and/or rate reversions.
> 14. If, in connection with an exchange of the Car due to a mechanical issue, Hertz is unable to provide You with a Car eligible for participation in the Lyft Driver Rental Program, you may not use such replacement Car to perform the "for hire" services contemplated by Item 2 above, but may return such replacement Car to the location from which the original (replaced) Car was rented during normal business hours for such location in order to exchange the replacement Car with a Car eligible for participation in the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> 15. You agree to indemnify, defend and hold Hertz and Lyft harmless from any and all losses, damages, liabilities, injuries, claims, demands, expenses and costs (including, without limitation, attorneys’ fees and expenses) which Hertz or Lyft may incur by reason of, or arising out of, Your (i) breach or violation of, or failure to observe or perform any term, provision or covenant of, the Agreement or this Addendum, or (ii) Your performance of services as a participating driver on the Lyft platform. This indemnification is in addition to, and not in lieu of, any indemnification by You set forth in the Agreement, and shall survive the termination of the Agreement.
> 16. You acknowledge and agree that You are not permitted to perform any work or service whatsoever for Hertz under the terms of the Lyft Driver Rental Program and warrant and represent that You shall not do so. You further acknowledge and agree that while participating in the Lyft Driver Rental Program You are not nor shall You be construed in any way as an employee, contractor, or vendor of Hertz, that You shall not be entitled to any benefits accorded by Hertz to its employee, including without limitation workers compensation, disability insurance, vacation, or sick pay, and that the only relationship You have with Hertz is as defined under the terms of the Lyft Driver Rental Program.
> 17. You expressly agree that Lyft shall be a third party beneficiary of this Addendum for purposes of enforcing Sections 4, 5, 6, 13 and 15 hereof against You.
> 18. You acknowledge and agree that, in the event You fail to satisfy the requirements provided by Lyft in connection with the Lyft Driver Rental Program, and therefore do not qualify as a Qualified LRP Driver under the Lyft Rental Program with Hertz, You shall be charged the then-current market rate for the Car for the entire duration of the rental and will be required to return the Car. Those requirements include, without limitation:
>   1. Complete at least twenty (20) rides on the Lyft Platform for each calendar week during the rental period.
>   2. Comply with Lyft's terms of service and maintain good standing on the Lyft platform at all times during the rental period; and
>   3. Comply with the terms of the Agreement as modified by this Addendum for such rental.
> 
> 
> 19. You acknowledge and agree that in the event that your prior scheduled rental due date has passed, and you have kept your rental vehicle, the rental period will be automatically extended for an additional week, for a maximum of 7 weeks, provided that you have sufficient funds in Your account with Lyft and continue to be in compliance with the Agreement as modified by this Addendum. However, in the event you receive notice to return your rental vehicle for it being late, you must do so. You acknowledge that you have no right to extension of a rental and Hertz may refuse to extend Your rental or permit you to rent again (under this program or for any other purpose) for any reason, including without limitation excessive mileage or wear and tear on the Car. If a rental is not extended at the discretion of Hertz, regular late fees will apply.

### Assistant
> Yep — this cleaner numbered version is much easier to use. Here’s the **dispute map** from the actual addendum language.
> 
> ## Core takeaway
> 
> This addendum is **bad for driver leverage overall**, but it gives you **three useful pressure points**:
> 
> 1. **LDW is expressly included**
> 2. **Optional insurance products may not even be available**
> 3. **The car must be usable as a Lyft Driver Rental Program vehicle**
> 
> So the argument is not “I owe nothing because Hertz sucks.”
> 
> The argument is:
> 
> > Hertz charged me for add-ons that appear inconsistent with the Lyft Driver Rental Program terms, failed to provide a usable Lyft-eligible vehicle during the sticker/key/battery issue, and then attempted to collect full program charges despite the rental being materially impaired.
> 
> That’s the clean lane.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Clauses that help you
> 
> ## Section 7 — LDW included
> 
> This is the big one.
> 
> It says:
> 
> > “LDW will be included with Your rental…”
> 
> That means if Hertz separately charged you for **LDW**, you need them to explain exactly what that charge was.
> 
> Your question to Hertz:
> 
> > If LDW is included with the Lyft Driver Rental Program rental under Section 7 of the addendum, why was I charged a separate LDW amount and tax on LDW?
> 
> This is your strongest contract-text argument.
> 
> But don’t overstate it. Section 7 also says there is a **$1,000 deductible**. So do **not** claim “full coverage.” Say:
> 
> > LDW/damage protection was represented as included, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms.
> 
> That’s accurate and harder for them to dodge.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Section 8 — optional insurance may not be available
> 
> Section 8 says you may not be eligible to purchase optional insurance products from Hertz, including:
> 
> - LIS
> - PAI / PEC
> - ESP
> 
> This helps you challenge any “optional product” charge.
> 
> Ask:
> 
> > Was the LDW or Premium Roadside charge mandatory, optional, or separately elected? If optional, please provide the signed authorization or digital acceptance showing I knowingly selected it.
> 
> This is where they either produce proof or they look sloppy.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Section 14 — replacement must be Lyft-eligible
> 
> This section says if Hertz gives you a replacement car that is not eligible for the Lyft Driver Rental Program, you cannot use it for Lyft.
> 
> That confirms something important:
> 
> > The whole value of the rental is that it must be Lyft-eligible.
> 
> So if the plate/sticker issue, key issue, battery issue, or branch delay made the car unusable or not safely operable for Lyft, you argue:
> 
> > Hertz failed to provide the core thing being rented: a safe, compliant, Lyft-eligible vehicle.
> 
> That is better than just saying “I was inconvenienced.”
> 
> ---
> 
> # Clauses that hurt you
> 
> ## Section 2 — Lyft only
> 
> You cannot frame the rental as something you needed for Uber, DoorDash, GoPuff, Roadie, etc.
> 
> Bad wording:
> 
> > I needed this car to do gig work.
> 
> Better wording:
> 
> > I rented the vehicle specifically through the Lyft Driver Rental Program to perform Lyft rides.
> 
> Keep it Lyft-only. Don’t hand them an easy “program violation” defense.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Section 6 — broad collection rights
> 
> This section lets Hertz/Lyft deduct:
> 
> - rental charges
> - damage fees
> - tolls
> - tickets
> - deductibles
> - additional rental amounts
> 
> So your fight is **not** “they had no right to deduct money.”
> 
> Your fight is:
> 
> > The amounts deducted included unauthorized or improperly disclosed charges, and they failed to adjust for periods where the vehicle was not usable as promised.
> 
> That’s tighter.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Section 13 — return/stolen vehicle risk
> 
> This clause is dangerous.
> 
> If they tell you to return the car and you do not, they can escalate. So everything needs to be documented in writing.
> 
> Your safe wording:
> 
> > I am not refusing to return the vehicle. I am requesting written clarification of the disputed charges, return/swap instructions, and account correction so this can be resolved safely and without additional improper penalties.
> 
> Do not sound like you are holding the car hostage. That would be bad strategy.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## Section 18 — 20 rides per week
> 
> They can charge market rate if you do not complete at least **20 Lyft rides per week**.
> 
> Your counterpoint is:
> 
> > Hertz’s unresolved sticker/plate and vehicle/key/battery issues interfered with my ability to complete the required Lyft rides.
> 
> This matters. You’re not saying “I just didn’t drive.” You’re saying the rental provider created the barrier.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The clean dispute theory
> 
> Use this:
> 
> > The Lyft Driver Rental Program addendum states that LDW is included with the rental, subject to a $1,000 deductible and program terms. Despite that, I was charged separate LDW-related amounts, including tax on LDW, without clear authorization or explanation. I was also charged Premium Roadside even though roadside-related support was represented as part of the program materials. In addition, Hertz failed to timely resolve plate/sticker and vehicle/key/battery issues, materially interfering with my ability to safely use the vehicle for Lyft and meet the program’s weekly ride requirements. I am requesting an itemized ledger, proof of authorization for all optional charges, removal/refund of unauthorized add-ons, and an adjustment for the period the vehicle was not usable as a compliant Lyft rental.
> 
> That’s the argument. Clean. Boring. Effective.
> 
> ---
> 
> # What to ask Hertz for
> 
> Send a written request for:
> 
> | Demand | Why it matters |
> |---|---|
> | Full itemized ledger | Shows every charge, tax, deduction, payment, deposit, and hold |
> | Signed/digital authorization for LDW | Forces proof that you agreed to a separate LDW charge |
> | Explanation of Section 7 LDW | They must reconcile “LDW included” with separate LDW billing |
> | Proof Premium Roadside was optional and accepted | Same consent problem |
> | Credit for unusable rental days | Sticker/key/battery issue impaired the rental |
> | Written return/swap instructions | Protects you from Section 13 escalation |
> | Confirmation no market-rate reversion | Protects you from Section 18 if their delay caused ride shortfall |
> 
> ---
> 
> # Best exact line to use
> 
> > Section 7 of the Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum states that LDW “will be included” with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms. Please explain why I was charged separate LDW-related amounts, including tax on LDW, and provide the signed or digital authorization showing I knowingly agreed to that separate charge.
> 
> That is the dagger. Use that.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Don’t get distracted
> 
> Do **not** lead with the medical episode, hotels, hygiene, sleeping in the car, or emotional impact.
> 
> Those matter, but they are secondary. Lead with contract/billing/usability.
> 
> Order should be:
> 
> 1. **Unauthorized or unexplained charges**
> 2. **Program documents say LDW included**
> 3. **Vehicle not usable/compliant**
> 4. **Hertz delay caused inability to earn/meet ride requirement**
> 5. **Hardship/safety consequences**
> 
> Facts first. Pain second. Otherwise they will treat it like a customer service rant instead of a billing/program dispute.

### Assistant
> Girl. This is **much stronger than before**. You now have actual screenshots showing the contradiction.
> 
> ## What the evidence proves
> 
> ### 1. Lyft advertised “insurance” as included
> 
> Your screenshot says under **Drive worry-free**:
> 
> > “Every plan includes unlimited Lyft miles, standard maintenance, and insurance.”
> 
> That is huge. Not “available.” Not “optional.” **Includes.**
> 
> So your argument becomes:
> 
> > Lyft represented insurance/protection as included in every plan. Hertz/Lyft then charged additional loss/collision damage waiver fees as separate vehicle/equipment charges without clear explanation or authorization.
> 
> Do **not** say “they promised full coverage.” Say:
> 
> > “Insurance/protection was represented as included, subject to program terms.”
> 
> That keeps you accurate.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. The addendum says LDW is included
> 
> Section 7 says:
> 
> > “LDW will be included with Your rental…”
> 
> Now your Lyft billing summary separately shows:
> 
> - **May 25 – May 31**
>   - Vehicle & equipment charges: **$48.00**
>   - “Loss/collision damage waiver”
>   - Other rental taxes: **$6.24**
>   - Tax on loss/collision damage waiver
> 
> - **Jun 1 – Jun 7**
>   - Vehicle & equipment charges: **$84.00**
>   - “Loss/collision damage waiver”
>   - Other rental taxes: **$10.92**
>   - Tax on loss/collision damage waiver
> 
> - Current week estimate:
>   - Base: **$296.00**
>   - Hertz LLDW: **$72.00**
>   - Tax on loss/collision damage waiver: **$9.36**
>   - Final balance: **$429.15**
> 
> That is the contradiction.
> 
> ## The clean billing issue
> 
> Your cleanest point is:
> 
> > If LDW is included under the Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum, why is Hertz/Lyft separately charging me for LLDW/loss-collision damage waiver?
> 
> That is not emotional. That is not messy. That is contract + receipt. Beautiful.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Your evidence table
> 
> | Evidence | What it supports |
> |---|---|
> | Lyft page: “Every plan includes… insurance” | You had reason to believe protection was included |
> | Addendum Section 7: “LDW will be included” | Contract text supports included LDW |
> | May 25–31 summary: $48 LDW + $6.24 tax | Separate LDW charge occurred |
> | Jun 1–7 summary: $84 LDW + $10.92 tax | Separate LDW charge increased |
> | Current week: Hertz LLDW $72 + $9.36 tax | Ongoing separate waiver charge |
> | Deposit screen: $350 deposit held until end | Deposit was not applied to weekly balance unless refund calculation/end-of-rental |
> | Billing history says “No history yet” despite weekly summaries | App billing recordkeeping appears incomplete/confusing |
> | Ride count history: 20, 24, 46 rides | You were meeting or exceeding weekly ride minimums during key weeks |
> 
> ---
> 
> # Important: the ride minimum actually helps you
> 
> You had:
> 
> - May 18–24: **34 rides**
> - May 25–31: **20 rides**
> - Jun 1–7: **24 rides**
> - Jun 8–14: **46 rides**
> 
> So Hertz/Lyft cannot easily say you were just failing the program. You met the required **20 rides/week** for the relevant weeks.
> 
> That matters because Section 18 says failure to complete 20 rides can trigger market-rate charges. Your evidence shows you were compliant.
> 
> Use this line:
> 
> > I met or exceeded the 20-ride weekly requirement during the relevant weeks, including 20 rides for May 25–31, 24 rides for June 1–7, and 46 rides for June 8–14.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The deposit issue
>

> 
> > “We’ll hold onto your deposit until you end your rental.”
> 
> And:
> 
> > charges owed may be deducted from the deposit refund at the time of refund calculation.
> 
> So the deposit is **not** a normal weekly credit. Annoying, but likely allowed.
> 
> Do not waste your strongest energy arguing “they should have used the deposit now.” That’s not your best lane.
> 
> Your better deposit argument is narrower:
> 
> > I paid a $350 deposit, and Lyft’s own app states charges may be deducted from the deposit refund calculation after the rental ends. Please provide a full accounting showing how the deposit, holds, weekly deductions, LDW/LLDW charges, taxes, and any claimed balance will be reconciled.

Section 7 of the Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum states that LDW “will be included” with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms. > 
> That is stronger because it proves this was **not automatically part of the base rental plan**. If it were mandatory, it would have been on **Week 1** too. Exactly.
> 
> ## The clean timeline
> 
> Use this structure. Do **not** lead with the whole life-collapse story. Lead with the billing defect.
> 
> | Date / Week | What happened | Why it matters |
> |---|---|---|
> | **May 18** | Paid $350 deposit | Deposit was separate, held until rental ends |
> | **May 19-ish / Week 1: May 18–24** | Rental begins; no LDW/LLDW charge appears | Shows LDW was not automatically part of weekly rental billing |

> ## 4. Key fob battery / AAA / unusable car day
> 
> This is strong.
> 
> | Item | Amount / credit |
> |---|---:|
> | Key fob battery | **~$16–$17** |
> | One unusable rental day credit | at least **1 day base + fees/taxes** |
> | Roadside failure / Premium Roadside issue | reverse any roadside charges if billed |
> 
> Your best wording:
> 
> > I was charged for rental use and/or roadside-related services during a period when the vehicle was unusable because the key fob / lockout / vehicle battery issue prevented access and operation. I had to use my own AAA and pay out of pocket for the key fob battery. AAA tested the vehicle battery and advised it was bad, but Hertz did not address it.
> 
> ---
>

> 
> Goal:
> 
> - vehicle swap or battery inspection/replacement
> - written note that LDW/LLDW removal was requested
> - written note of sticker issue / return notices / no swap
> - reimbursement for key fob battery

> 
> Use this only if Call 1 fails or stalls.

> # What to say today
> 
> Use this. Don’t over-explain. Read it like a script.
> 
> :::writing{variant="standard" id="46829"}
> I need to open a formal billing and vehicle-service dispute for my Lyft Express Drive rental through Hertz.
> 
> The first rental week, May 18 through May 24, did not include any LDW, LLDW, or loss/collision damage waiver charge. Starting May 25 through May 31, a Loss/Collision Damage Waiver charge appeared for $48.00 plus $6.24 tax. The next week, June 1 through June 7, it appeared again for $84.00 plus $10.92 tax. The current week still shows Hertz LLDW for $72.00 plus $9.36 tax even after I asked Hertz to remove it. I am also aware the June 8 through June 14 rental reconciliation includes this disputed charge.
> 
> I did not authorize LDW or LLDW. The fact that it was not charged during the first rental week proves it was not automatically required as part of the base rental. Lyft’s Express Drive materials state that insurance/protection is included, and the Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum states that LDW is included with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms.
> 
> I am requesting immediate removal of current and future LDW/LLDW charges, credit or refund of all LDW/LLDW charges and related taxes, and written proof of any signed or digital authorization Hertz claims allowed this charge to be added after the rental began.
> 
> I also need the applicable Express Drive rate card reviewed. Lyft advised that the rental rate may decrease after the qualifying rental period or renewal period. Please explain why I am still being charged a $296 base rate and credit any difference if a lower rate should have applied.
> 
> Separately, I am requesting reimbursement for the key fob battery I had to purchase and credit for the day the vehicle was unusable due to the lockout / key fob / vehicle battery issue. I had to use my own AAA because the rental roadside process could not assist while the needed confirmation information was locked inside the vehicle. AAA tested the vehicle battery and advised it was bad and needed replacement. Hertz was informed, but the issue was not resolved with a swap or repair plan.
> 
> I also need the overdraft fees caused by the disputed charges documented. I currently have four $36 overdraft fees with Old National and two $36 overdraft fees with Chase, totaling $216. These fees resulted from the disputed rental charges being pulled while the account issue remained unresolved.
> 
> Please open a formal dispute case, provide the case number, and tell me where to send screenshots, receipts, and bank fee documentation.

### Assistant
> Yes. This is the right structure: **primary hard credits first, secondary damages second, hardship/context third.** That keeps it credible instead of turning into a rage-scroll.
> 
> Here’s the repackaged version.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Claim structure
> 
> ## Section 1 — Direct billing errors and out-of-pocket costs
> 
> These are the strongest, most concrete amounts.
> 
> | Item | Amount |
> |---|---:|
> | May 25–May 31 unauthorized LDW + tax | **$54.24** |
> | Jun 1–Jun 7 unauthorized LDW + tax | **$94.92** |
> | Jun 8–Jun 14 unauthorized LDW + tax, expected/known from support | **$94.92** |
> | Current week LLDW + tax still showing | **$81.36** |
> | Key fob battery | **~$16–$17** |
> | Lyft ride to battery place | **$7.00** |
> | **Direct hard-credit demand** | **about $348–$349** |
> 
> If the key fob battery was exactly $16.00, the direct total is:
> 
> > **$348.44**
> 
> If it was $17.00:
> 
> > **$349.44**
> 
> ## Section 2 — Bank fees caused by disputed charges
> 
> | Account | Fees | Total |
> |---|---:|---:|
> | Old National | 4 × $36 | **$144** |
> | Chase | 2 × $36 | **$72** |
> | **Total overdraft fee reimbursement requested** |  | **$216** |
> 
> Hard + overdraft total:
> 
> > **about $564–$565 before hotel/food/gas/lost-use credits.**
> 
> ## Section 3 — Secondary reimbursement / service failure costs
> 
> These are fair to request, but keep them in a separate bucket:
> 
> - Two hotel nights caused by being required to come to Indianapolis for a sticker/swap that was not ready.
> - Food/per diem while stranded.
> - Gas/travel caused by repeated branch trips.
> - Rental credit for days the vehicle was not safely usable because of expired/invalid sticker concern, lockout, key fob failure, and bad battery.
> - Any Premium Roadside charges, because the roadside process failed when you actually needed it.
> 
> ## Section 4 — Serious consequential harm / escalation context
> 
> No dollar value yet. Just document it:
> 
> - You were stranded away from home for nearly two weeks.
> - You lost caregiver income and had to resign from the caregiver position because you could not reliably return.
> - Your mother’s care was disrupted and she was hospitalized.
> - You experienced heat exposure/medical symptoms during the lockout/battery incident.
> - You had to walk roughly two miles to access help/phone/roadside support.
> - Hertz/Lyft repeatedly redirected responsibility between each other instead of resolving the account and vehicle issues.
> 
> Do **not** say “you almost killed my mom.” Say:
> 
> > “This created a serious and foreseeable caregiving disruption while my mother was medically vulnerable.”
> 
> That hits harder because it sounds controlled.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Formal dispute version
> 
> :::writing{variant="document" id="19384"}
> Subject: Formal Dispute — Unauthorized LDW/LLDW Charges, Vehicle Service Failure, and Related Damages
> 
> I am submitting a formal dispute regarding my Lyft Express Drive rental through Hertz.
> 
> The core issue is that LDW/LLDW charges were added after my rental began without my authorization, continued after I disputed them, and remain on the account even after I asked Hertz to remove them.
> 
> My first rental week, May 18–May 24, did not include any LDW, LLDW, or loss/collision damage waiver charge. That week only showed the base rental, vehicle license fee, and taxes. Starting the second week, LDW/LLDW charges appeared.
> 
> Disputed LDW/LLDW charges currently identified:
> 
> 1. May 25–May 31:
> Loss/Collision Damage Waiver: $48.00  
> Tax on LDW: $6.24  
> Subtotal: $54.24
> 
> 2. Jun 1–Jun 7:
> Loss/Collision Damage Waiver: $84.00  
> Tax on LDW: $10.92  
> Subtotal: $94.92
> 
> 3. Jun 8–Jun 14:
> Lyft support confirmed the disputed LDW/LLDW charge is also on this week’s rental reconciliation. Based on the prior full-week charge, I am estimating this at $84.00 plus $10.92 tax, subject to final summary confirmation.  
> Estimated subtotal: $94.92
> 
> 4. Current week:
> Hertz LLDW: $72.00  
> Tax on LDW/LLDW: $9.36  
> Subtotal: $81.36
> 
> Known/expected LDW/LLDW dispute total so far: $325.44
> 
> This charge was not present during the first rental week, which shows it was not automatically required as a separate weekly charge. I did not authorize it to be added later. Lyft’s Express Drive materials represent insurance/protection as included, and the Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum states that LDW is included with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms.
> 
> I am requesting:
> 
> 1. Immediate removal of all current and future LDW/LLDW charges.
> 2. Refund or credit of all unauthorized LDW/LLDW charges and related taxes.
> 3. Written proof of any signed, initialed, or digital authorization Hertz claims allowed LDW/LLDW to be added after the rental began.
> 4. A full itemized rental ledger showing base rental, LDW/LLDW, roadside, taxes, deposits, holds, deductions, payments, and balances.
> 5. Review of the applicable Express Drive rate schedule, including whether my base rate should have decreased after the qualifying rental or renewal period.
> 
> I am also requesting reimbursement for direct out-of-pocket costs caused by the vehicle/key/roadside failure:
> 
> - Key fob battery purchased out of pocket: approximately $16–$17
> - Lyft ride to reach the battery location: $7.00
> 
> Direct hard-credit request so far: approximately $348–$349, before bank fees and other damages.
> 
> I am also requesting reimbursement of overdraft fees caused by the disputed charges and delayed correction. I currently have four $36 overdraft fees with Old National and two $36 overdraft fees with Chase, totaling $216. These fees resulted from disputed rental charges and balances being pulled from my accounts while the LDW/LLDW issue remained unresolved.
> 
> I am also requesting separate review and credit for the vehicle-service failure and stranded-driver issue.
> 
> Hertz required me to come to Indianapolis regarding the plate/sticker issue, but the sticker was not available when I arrived. I was told to come back, but I could not safely or reasonably drive three hours back to Evansville and three hours back to Indianapolis with limited gas, limited funds, and concern that the vehicle could be stopped because of the plate/sticker issue. My Lyft earnings for that period reflect that I barely drove because I was concerned about operating the vehicle while the plate/sticker issue was unresolved.
> 
> Hertz also discussed swapping the vehicle, but the swap was not completed. I was told changes could not be made because of a balance, but that balance was directly affected by disputed LDW/LLDW charges that should not have been on the account in the first place. Later, when I returned again, I was given the sticker but the swap/battery issue was not resolved.
> 
> During the lockout/key/battery incident, the vehicle was unusable. I attempted to use the roadside support connected to the rental, but I could not complete the process because the required information was inside the locked vehicle. I ultimately had to use my own AAA. AAA tested the vehicle battery and advised that the vehicle battery was bad and needed replacement. I reported this to Hertz, but the issue was not resolved with a repair plan or swap. This means the same failure could happen again.
> 
> Because of these failures, I am requesting:
> 
> 1. Credit for the day the vehicle was unusable due to the lockout/key fob/battery issue.
> 2. Reimbursement of the key fob battery and related Lyft ride.
> 3. Reversal of any roadside-related charges if roadside was charged.
> 4. Review of hotel, food/per diem, gas, and travel costs caused by being required to come to Indianapolis without Hertz having the sticker/swap ready.
> 5. Written confirmation of the vehicle battery inspection/replacement or a vehicle swap.
> 
> This situation caused serious additional harm. I was stranded away from home for an extended period while repeatedly being redirected between Hertz and Lyft. I lost access to funds because earnings were being absorbed by disputed rental charges. I was unable to reliably return home, which disrupted my caregiver work and contributed to the loss of that caregiver position. My medically vulnerable mother’s care was also disrupted during this period, and she was hospitalized. I also experienced heat exposure and medical symptoms during the vehicle lockout/battery incident and had to walk roughly two miles to access help.
> 
> I am asking Hertz and Lyft to stop redirecting responsibility between each other. The charges are appearing through the Lyft Express Drive rental system, but they originate from the Hertz rental record. I need a formal dispute case opened, a case number, written confirmation of where to send documentation, and a clear decision on credits, refunds, and vehicle resolution.
> :::

> # My blunt guidance
> 
> Lead with **money math**, not trauma.
> 
> Order:
> 
> 1. **LDW/LLDW unauthorized charges**
> 2. **Overdraft fees**
> 3. **Key fob + Lyft ride + unusable vehicle day**
> 4. **Hotel/food/gas**
> 5. **Caregiver/mother/heat exposure as escalation context**
> 
> That’s how you make them pay attention instead of mentally labeling it “complicated customer meltdown.” Keep the knife clean.

### Assistant
> Oh. **This is the smoking gun.**
> 
> You have **two Hertz rental agreements for the exact same rental record, one minute apart**:
> 
> - **9:49 AM:** LDW + Premium Roadside are listed as **Accepted**
> - **9:50 AM:** LDW + Premium Roadside are **gone**
> 
> Same rental record. Same car. Same rental time. Same return time.
> 
> That proves Hertz **can remove it**, and it proves the corrected contract exists.
> 
> ## What this adds to your case
> 
> ### Rental Record: **594402524**
> 
> | Time | Additional products | Estimated total | Authorization |
> |---|---|---:|---:|
> | **Jun 12, 9:49 AM** | LDW **$76.93** + Premium Roadside **$7.07** | **$448.78** | **$649.00** |
> | **Jun 12, 9:50 AM** | **No LDW. No Premium Roadside.** | **$350.50** | **$551.00** |
> | **Difference** | Add-ons removed | **$98.28 lower** | **$98 lower auth** |
> 
> ## Why this matters
> 
> This gives you a new, sharper argument:
> 
> > Hertz generated a corrected rental agreement on Jun 12 at 9:50 AM for Rental Record 594402524 with no LDW and no Premium Roadside. Therefore, any Lyft/Hertz system continuing to charge LDW/LLDW or Premium Roadside after that corrected agreement is inconsistent with Hertz’s own rental agreement.
> 
> That is stronger than “I asked them to remove it.”
> 
> Now it is:
> 
> > **They did remove it. Their own corrected agreement proves it. The billing system kept charging anyway.**
> 
> That is big.
> 
> ## Updated direct dispute amount
> 
> We now have one more hard amount:
> 
> | Category | Amount |
> |---|---:|
> | May 25–May 31 unauthorized LDW + tax | **$54.24** |
> | Jun 1–Jun 7 unauthorized LDW + tax | **$94.92** |

> Fair. Use this version. **Do not read the whole complaint packet.** Live agents cannot process the whole saga. Your mission is **same-day vehicle resolution + documented case number**.
> 
> ## Live agent script — use this verbatim
> 
> :::writing{variant="standard" id="51482"}
> Hi, I need immediate help with a Lyft Express Drive Hertz rental. This is not just a billing question. The vehicle has now had a second battery failure after I already reported the issue.
> 
> The car is currently running because I had to jump/start it, but I am afraid to turn it off because the battery is failing again. I am burning fuel just to keep the car from dying. I need this documented as a repeat mechanical failure and I need one of three things today:
> 
> 1. confirmation of a same-day vehicle swap,
> 2. authorization for local battery replacement with reimbursement,
> 3. or tow/roadside assistance with rental downtime credit.
> 
> I am willing to cooperate and come in if needed, but last time I was told to come in, I ended up stranded for an extended period without a completed resolution. I need confirmation before I drive long distance again in an unreliable vehicle.
> 
> Please open a case and give me the case number.
> :::
> 
> ## If they say “you need to go to the counter”
> 
> Say:
> 
> > I understand, but I need this documented first. The vehicle has already failed twice. I need confirmation that the branch can swap or repair it today before I drive there, because I cannot safely shut the vehicle off and I may get stranded again.
> 
> ## If they say “call Lyft”
> 
> Say:
> 
> > Lyft told me Hertz controls the vehicle and rental record. I need Hertz to document the mechanical failure and tell me whether Hertz is authorizing a swap, tow, or battery replacement.
> 
> ## If they say “call Hertz” and you’re talking to Lyft
> 
> Say:
> 
> > Hertz says the rental charges and account status flow through Lyft. I need Lyft to document that the vehicle is currently unreliable, the battery has failed again, and I am requesting rental downtime credit and escalation through Express Drive.
> 
> ## If they refuse to guarantee a swap
> 
> Say:
> 
> > Then please document that Hertz/Lyft cannot confirm a same-day repair or swap even though the vehicle has repeated battery failure. I need the case number and the name or ID of this interaction.
> 
> ## Do not hang up without these
> 
> Get:
> 
> - case number
> - agent name or ID
> - exact instruction they gave you
> - whether they authorized swap, tow, or local repair
> - whether downtime/rental credit was noted
> - whether fuel loss from forced idling was noted
> 
> ## Your anchor line
> 
> > The vehicle has failed twice. I am not refusing to cooperate; I need a confirmed safe resolution before I risk being stranded again.
> 
> That’s the line. Keep dragging them back to it.

> RENTAL AGREEMENT TERMS AND CONDITIONS
> 
> THESE TERMS AND CONDITIONS, THE RENTAL RECORD SIGNED BY YOU AND ANY OTHER DOCUMENTS WHICH YOU ARE REQUIRED TO SIGN WHEN YOU RENT THE CAR, AND WHICH MAY BE SIGNED ELECTRONICALLY, WHICH BOTH YOU AND HERTZ AGREE SHALL BE TREATED AS ORIGINAL, TOGETHER CONSTITUTE THE AGREEMENT (“THIS AGREEMENT”) FOR THE RENTAL OF THE VEHICLE IDENTIFIED ON THE RENTAL RECORD, INCLUDING ALL OF ITS PARTS (“CAR”). THIS AGREEMENT IS BETWEEN YOU AND THE HERTZ COMPANY WHICH IS IDENTIFIED ON THE RENTAL RECORD (“HERTZ”).
> 
> 1.     NATURE OF THIS AGREEMENT
> 
> You are obtaining solely a bailment that allows You to use the Car as permitted by this Agreement. You acknowledge that the Car is owned by Hertz. No one other than Hertz may transfer the Car or any rights or obligations under this Agreement. Any attempted transfer or sublease of the Car by anyone other than Hertz is void. Neither You nor any Authorized Operators are agents of Hertz. No one may service or repair the Car without Hertz’ prior express approval. HERTZ MAKES NO EXPRESS OR IMPLIED WARRANTIES, INCLUDING ANY WARRANTY OF MERCHANTABILITY OR THAT THE CAR IS FIT FOR ANY PARTICULAR PURPOSE.
> 
> 2.     WHO MAY OPERATE THE CAR
> 
> Only You and, with Your permission, the following persons (“Authorized Operators”), may operate the Car: (a) For rentals commencing in the states of CA and IA, Your spouse and Your employer, employees and fellow employees incidental to their business duties; (b) for rentals (“Replacement Rentals”) which are designated as replacement rentals on the Rental Record, any person specifically named as an insured on Your automobile policy; and (c) any other person who meets Hertz’ qualifications and who signs an Additional Authorized Operator form at the time of rental. Except as provided in the following sentence, all Authorized Operators must be at least 20 years old and have a valid driver’s license from a jurisdiction acceptable to Hertz. Charges for Authorized Operators under 25 may apply. For rentals which commence in Michigan and New York, persons between the ages of 18 and 24 who meet Hertz’ other qualifications and who sign an Additional Authorized Operator form at the time of rental may be Authorized Operators; in such cases, an Underage Differential Charge will be assessed. Except to the extent necessary for valet parking or in an emergency as permitted by law, no other persons are permitted to operate the Car; for purposes hereof, an “emergency” shall mean urgent circumstances under the laws of the jurisdiction in which the alleged emergency occurred. With respect to persons who must sign an Additional Authorized Operator form, other qualifications may, at Hertz’ discretion, be in effect at the time and place of rental; and, where permitted by law, Hertz may impose an additional fee for such persons. By operating the Car (whether or not an Additional Authorized Operator form is completed), an Authorized Operator will be deemed jointly and severally responsible for Your obligations under this Agreement related to the Car, as well as for any obligations that this Agreement directly imposes on an Authorized Operator of the Car (for example: the obligations contained in paragraph 9).
> 
> 3.     RETURN
> 
> ORDINARY WEAR DUE TO REASONABLE USE EXCEPTED, YOU MUST RETURN THE CAR TO HERTZ IN THE SAME CONDITION IT IS IN WHEN YOU RECEIVE IT. ORDINARY WEAR IS THE MINOR DEGRADATION OF VEHICLE CONDITION DUE TO NORMAL USE. THIS INCLUDES REGULAR TIRE TREAD WEAR, LIMITED SAND PITTING TO THE PAINT OF THE VEHICLE, AND PAINT TRANSFER OR SCUFFS THAT DO NOT BREAK THE SURFACE OF THE VEHICLE’S PAINT.IF YOU EXCEED 3500 MILES DRIVEN IN A 30 DAY PERIOD YOUR RENTAL PRIVILEGES MAY BE REVOKED DUE TO EXCESSIVE WEAR AND TEAR. YOU MUST RETURN THE CAR TO HERTZ BY THE DUE DATE SPECIFIED ON THE RENTAL RECORD, OR SOONER IF DEMANDED BY HERTZ. IF AN EXTENSION HAS BEEN GRANTED, THEN YOU MUST RETURN BY THE EXTENDED DUE DATE.     IN NO EVENT MAY YOU KEEP THE CAR FOR MORE THAN THIRTY (30) DAYS (IN NEW JERSEY, OHIO AND SOUTH DAKOTA, 28 DAYS), UNLESS AUTHORIZED IN WRITING BY HERTZ. A RETURN CHANGE FEE WILL APPLY TO ANY CHANGE IN YOUR SCHEDULED RETURN DATE, TIME OR LOCATION. IF YOU RETURN THE CAR BEFORE OR AFTER YOUR SCHEDULED RETURN DATE AND TIME, YOUR BASE RENTAL RATE WILL BE ADJUSTED TO REFLECT THE MODIFIED RENTAL DURATION AT OUR THEN-CURRENT PRICING, WHICH MAY BE HIGHER THAN THE RATE AT WHICH YOU ORIGINALLY BOOKED. IN ADDITION, IF YOU FAIL TO TIMELY NOTIFY HERTZ OF SUCH CHANGE, HERTZ WILL CHARGE YOU AN EARLY/LATE RETURN FEE. IF YOU FAIL TO RETURN THE CAR BY THE DUE DATE SPECIFIED ON THE RENTAL RECORD, HERTZ WILL COMMENCE ITS OVERUE RENTAL PROCESS AND CHARGE YOU FOR ALL RELATED EXPENSES.   AS PART OF HERTZ’S OVERDUE PROCESS, YOU EXPRESSLY CONSENT AND AGREE THAT HERTZ MAY USE ELECTRONIC OR VERBAL MEANS TO CONTACT YOU IN ORDER TO URGE YOU TO RETURN THE CAR. YOU AGREE THAT HERTZ MAY USE ANY AVAILABLE EMAIL ADDRESS OR TELEPHONE NUMBER TO CONTACT YOU, INCLUDING MANUAL CALLING, VOICE MESSAGES, TEXT MESSAGES, EMAILS OR AUTOMATIC TELEPHONE DIALING SYSTEMS.  IF YOU DO NOT RETURN THE CAR WHEN REQUIRED BY THIS AGREEMENT, THEN AFTER HERTZ SENDS YOU A WRITTEN DEMAND TO RETURN IT, SENT TO YOUR ADDRESS SHOWN ON THE RENTAL RECORD OR OTHERWISE PROVIDED TO HERTZ, HERTZ MAY, AT YOUR EXPENSE, UTILIZE A THIRD-PARTY REPOSSESSION VENDOR TO RECOVER THE CAR WHERE AND WHEN IT IS LOCATED. YOU WILL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR ALL EXPENSES INCURRED BY HERTZ IN ATTEMPTING TO REPOSSESS THE CAR.  THE CAR MAY BE EQUIPPED WITH MANUFACTURER OR THIRD-PARTY IN-VEHICLE TECHNOLOGIES AND TELEMATICS DEVICES, INCLUDING GLOBAL POSITIONING TECHNOLOGY, OR OTHER TELEMATICS SYSTEMS AND A TRANSMITTER THAT ALLOWS HERTZ TO TRACK OR OTHERWISE LOCATE THE CAR TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY LAW AND PRIVACY IS NOT GUARANTEED. TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY LAW, YOU AUTHORIZE HERTZ TO COLLECT, USE AND DISCLOSE DATA OBTAINED DURING THE COURSE OF YOUR RENTAL FROM SUCH TECHNOLOGIES AND DEVICES FOR A NUMBER OF PURPOSES RELATED TO YOUR VEHICLE’S RETURN, INCLUDING WITHOUT LIMITATION TO LOCATE THE VEHICLE DURING YOUR RENTAL IF THE VEHICLE IS LOST, STOLEN, OR OVERDUE, TO DISABLE THE CAR AND TO ASSIST IN THE REPOSSESSION OF THE CAR, TO DETERMINE THE TIME OF THE VEHICLE’S DEPARTURE FROM AND RETURN TO THE HERTZ RENTAL LOCATION, TO ESTIMATE THE LEVELS OF FUEL IN THE TANK UPON RETURN TO THE HERTZ RENTAL LOCATION, AND AS OTHERWISE PERMITTED BY APPLICABLE LAW. FOR MORE INFORMATION ABOUT HOW HERTZ MAY COLLECT, USE AND DISCLOSE INFORMATION COLLECTED THROUGH THESE TECHNOLOGIES IN A MANNER THAT IDENTIFIES YOU, PLEASE REVIEW OUR PRIVACY POLICY AS DESCRIBED IN SECTION 14 BELOW.
> 
> IF THE CAR IS FOUND ILLEGALLY PARKED OR APPARENTLY ABANDONED, OR IF THE CAR IS USED OR OBTAINED AS PROHIBITED UNDER PARAGRAPH 5, THEN HERTZ MAY RECOVER THE CAR WITHOUT DEMAND. TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY LAW, YOU WAIVE ANY RIGHT TO A HEARING OR TO RECEIVE ANY NOTICE OR LEGAL PROCESS AS A PRE-CONDITION FOR HERTZ RECOVERING THE CAR.
> 
> IN THE EVENT YOU HAVE NOT RETURNED THE CAR AS REQUIRED BY THIS AGREEMENT, AS A MEANS OF LAST RESORT, HERTZ RESERVES THE RIGHT TO REPORT THE CAR TO LAW ENFORCEMENT AS A THEFT AND TAKE ANY FURTHER ACTION NECESSARY IN CONNECTION WITH REPORTING THE CAR TO LAW ENFORCEMENT AS A THEFT.  IN THESE CIRCUMSTANCES, HERTZ RESERVES THE RIGHT TO SUSPEND YOUR RENTAL PRIVILEGES.
> 
> THE CAR WILL REMAIN SUBJECT TO THESE TERMS AND CONDITIONS UNTIL HERTZ HAS INSPECTED AND ACCEPTED IT; IF YOU RETURN THE CAR AFTER HOURS, (A) YOU ARE RESPONSIBLE FOR ANY DAMAGE TO THE CAR UNTIL HERTZ HAS INSPECTED AND ACCEPTED IT ON THE NEXT DAY THAT THE RETURN LOCATION IS OPEN FOR BUSINESS AND (B) TIME CHARGES, CHARGES FOR LDW, PAI/PEC AND LIS, AND ANY CHARGES FOR ADDITIONAL SERVICES OR OTHER CHARGES WHICH ARE STATED ON THE RENTAL RECORD AS A PERIODIC RATE, MAY CONTINUE TO ACCRUE UNTIL THE RETURN LOCATION REOPENS FOR BUSINESS.
> 
> YOU ACKNOWLEDGE THAT THE DATA DERIVED FROM THE IN-CAR TELEMATICS AND OTHER DEVICES MAY CONTAIN PERSONAL INFORMATION AND YOU AUTHORIZE HERTZ TO SHARE THAT DATA WITH THE DEVICE MANUFACTURER, THE ORIGINAL EQUIPMENT MANUFACTURER AND ITS AFFILIATES (COLLECTIVELY, “OEM”), SERVICE PROVIDERS, AND OTHER THIRD PARTIES TO WHOM HERTZ OR OEM GRANTS ACCESS. TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY LAW, YOU AUTHORIZE HERTZ,’ THE ORIGINAL EQUIPMENT MANUFACTURER’S (OEM) AND ANY THIRD-PARTY SERVICE PROVIDER’S USE OF THE TECHNOLOGY INCLUDED IN THE CAR, INCLUDING TO TRACK THE LOCATION OF THE CAR, TO DISABLE THE CAR AND TO ASSIST IN THE REPOSSESSION OF THE CAR, AND TO PROVIDE SERVICES TO YOU.
> 
> IT IS YOUR RESPONSIBILITY AT RETURN TO DELETE ANY BLUETOOTH SYNCED DEVICES OR DATA, NAVIGATION DATA, AND ALL OTHER PERSONAL INFORMATION INPUT OR PROVIDED BY YOU THROUGH USE OF IN VEHICLE EQUIPMENT OR FEATURES. YOU ACKNOWLEDGE AND AGREE THAT, TO THE EXTENT PERMITTED BY APPLICABLE LAW, HERTZ, THE OEM AND ANY THIRD-PARTY SERVICE PROVIDER MAY COLLECT, PROCESS, CHARGE ON THE BASIS OF, ADD TO YOUR CUSTOMER PROFILE AND TAKE DISCIPLINARY ACTION ON THE BASIS OF THE DATA DERIVED FROM VEHICLE TECHNOLOGIES AND TELEMATICS DEVICES, INCLUDING GLOBAL POSITIONING ACTIVITY. ACTIONS MAY INCLUDE SUSPENSION OR TERMINATION OF YOUR ABILITY TO CONTINUE TO RENT CARS FROM HERTZ OR ITS AFFILIATES. FOR INFORMATION ABOUT HOW HERTZ MAY COLLECT, USE AND DISCLOSE INFORMATION COLLECTED THROUGH THESE TECHNOLOGIES IN A MANNER THAT IDENTIFIES YOU, PLEASE REVIEW OUR PRIVACY POLICY AS DESCRIBED IN SECTION 14 BELOW.
> 
> YOU AUTHORIZE HERTZ TO PROVIDE PERSONAL INFORMATION ABOUT YOU AND EACH RENTAL YOU UNDERTAKE USING A CUSTOMER DISCOUNT PROGRAM (CDP) NUMBER OR OTHERWISE IN CONNECTION WITH THE RENTAL TO THE CDP SPONSOR OF THE RENTAL. HERTZ MAKES NO REPRESENTATIONS OR WARRANTIES AS TO THE USE OF SUCH INFORMATION BY THE CDP SPONSOR. YOUR RENTAL UNDER THIS AGREEMENT USING A CDP NUMBER IS YOUR CONSENT TO HERTZ TO DISCLOSE PERSONAL DATA TO THE CDP SPONSOR.
