> LIABILITY INSURANCE SUPPLEMENT (LIS)
> 
> SUMMARY OF COVERAGE
> 
> COVERAGE
> 
> If You elect to purchase LIS, coverage will be provided to You and any Authorized Operators under an excess automobile liability insurance policy provided by a third party.
> 
> LIMITS LIS provides protection from third party automobile liability claims for the difference between the liability protection limits provided under paragraph 10 and a maximum combined single limit of Three Hundred Thousand (US$300,000) Dollars for bodily injury, including death, and property damage. LIS also provides up to $100,000 in coverage for uninsured and underinsured motorist coverage for bodily injury per accident which includes any applicable minimum underlying state statutory limits. Uninsured/ underinsured protection is not available in California and does not cover losses caused by the negligence of the renter or any authorized operator. Uninsured/underinsured motorist coverage is excluded from LIS purchased from Hertz licensees unless expressly stated otherwise in writing at the rental location.
> 
> EXCLUSIONS
> 
> All exclusions, including claims arising from use of the Car as prohibited by this Agreement and claims by any of Your or any Authorized Operator’s family members related by blood, marriage or adoption who resides with You or the Authorized Operator, are set forth in the applicable policy, a copy of which is available at the corporate office.
> 
> HOW TO OBTAIN/DECLINE COVERAGE
> 
> If You elect LIS on the Rental Record, coverage will be provided during the rental period. The daily Charge for LIS, which appears on the Rental Record, is due for each full or partial rental day.
> 
> NOTICE OF CLAIM
> 
> If You have purchased LIS, LIS coverage will automatically attach to a claim once You have properly reported the accident in accordance with paragraph 12.
> 
> PERSONAL PROTECTION PACKAGE (PAI AND PEC) SUMMARY OF COVERAGE (PAI NOT AVAILABLE IN NY)
> 
> HOW TO OBTAIN PERSONAL PROTECTION PACKAGE
> 
> If You purchase the Personal Protection Package (PAI and PEC) on the Rental Record, coverage will be provided during the rental period.  Please note that the Personal Protection Package is not available separately and may only be taken in combination. The Daily Charge for the optional Personal Protection Package which appears on the Rental Record is due for each full and partial rental day. Coverage will be provided under a policy issued to Hertz.
> 
> PERSONAL ACCIDENT INSURANCE (PAI)
> 
> COVERAGE AND BENEFITS
> 
> The PAI policies provide coverage for bodily injury and death directly caused by an accident independent of all other causes where death occurs within twelve months following the bodily injury. The renter will be covered for any such accident during the rental period; passengers will also be covered, but only for accidents occurring while in, entering, or exiting the Car. Benefits include death benefits of US$175,000 for the renter *($100,000 in MN) and US$17,500 per passenger ($10,000 in MN); PAI also provides limited coverage for certain medical expenses (benefits are limited to $2,500 ($3,500 in MN), including ambulance expenses up to $250 ($150 in MN). Benefits for any one accident are limited to US $225,000 in the aggregate ($130,000 in MN). These benefits are payable without regard to any other benefits which may be due under any other insurance policy.
> 
> Medical expense coverage is available for bodily injury if within 30 days of the accident and upon the recommendation a qualified and licensed physician the insured is confined to a hospital, treated by a physician, transported to or from a hospital by a professional ambulance service and/or services rendered by a registered nurse, licensed practicing nurse, or nurse practitioner.
> 
> Coverage is subject to various exclusions, terms and conditions, which may vary by state, and is not available in New York. Please review your policy or certificate for detail.
> 
> EXCLUSIONS
> 
> The policy does not insure, nor will any payment of any kind be made for bodily injury caused wholly or partly, directly or
> 
> indirectly by (a) suicide, attempted suicide or intentionally self-inflicted injury, while insane or sane; (b) engagement in an illegal occupation or activity, committing or attempting to commit a criminal offense; (c) with respect to passengers, travel in any manner other than within the enclosed portion of the rental vehicle; (d) an accident that occurs while participating in a prearranged or organized race or testing of a vehicle; (e) bodily injury expected or intended from the standpoint of the
> 
> insured; (f) loss arising out of the operation of the rental vehicle by any driver who is not authorized operate the rental vehicle under the rental agreement; (g) violation of the rental agreement; (h) an accident which occurs while under the influence of alcohol or narcotics, unless prescribed and taken at the advice or direction of a physician; or (i) aircraft travel, except as a passenger on a licensed aircraft on a regularly scheduled flight.  No payment will be made if the renter converts the rental vehicle.
> 
> Please review your policy or certificate for additional exclusions and limitations.
> 
> NOTICE OF CLAIM
> 
> In the event of any occurrence likely to result in a claim for PAI benefits, immediate written notice should be given to Hertz. Hertz will provide You with a claim form and address of the insurance company which is providing coverage. You will have to submit the claim form to the insurance company together with Your Rental Record.
> 
> PERSONAL EFFECTS COVERAGE (PEC)
> 
> COVERAGE
> 
> PEC insures against risk of loss, theft or damage to help protect your personal belongings while renting from Hertz. PEC coverage applies throughout the entire rental period to owned personal property during transit, while in any hotel or building (other than the insured’s residence) or locked in a rental vehicle. PEC is insurance protection and pays in addition to any other policy You may have (such as a Homeowner’s policy). However, your benefits provided by other coverage may be affected by the PEC benefit. PEC includes those personal effects owned by You, other authorized drivers under the rental agreement, and your immediate family who permanently reside with you and are traveling with You during the rental period. Terms and conditions may vary by state. Please review your policy or certificate for detail.
> 
> LIMITS OF LIABILITY
> 
> Up to US$650 per person, and $1,950 in the aggregate for all claims during the rental period.
> 
> EXCLUSIONS
> 
> The policy does not insure: (a) any property not owned by the "insured" for other than their personal use, adornment, or enjoyment, (b) animals, "autos", "auto" equipment, motorcycles, water craft, motors, or other conveyances or their appurtenances, household or office furniture, business personal property or equity, contact lenses, glasses, artificial teeth or limbs, currency, coins, deeds, bullion, stamps, securities, negotiable instruments, debit or credit cards, fund transfer cards, tickets, documents or perishables, (c) against loss or damage caused by or resulting from or arising out of: (i) an "accident" which occurs while the "insured" is under the influence of alcohol or narcotics, unless prescribed by a physician, (ii) the use of a "rental vehicle" when such use is in violation of the conditions of the "rental agreement", (iii) the operation of the "rental vehicle" by any driver who is not an "insured", (iv) any "insureds" liability for damage to the "rental vehicle"; or (v) any loss of or damage to the "insureds" property, expected or intended from the standpoint of the "insured", (d) property while in the care, custody, or control of any common carrier, (e) loss or damage due to unexplained or mysterious disappearance, or (f) loss or damage due to theft unless reported to the police or other competent authority.  Please review your policy or certificate for additional exclusions and limitations.
>

> 
> All losses by theft must be reported to police or other authority within 24 hours of the robbery or theft, and if theft is from a vehicle the vehicle must show signs of forced entry.

> 
> In the event of any occurrence likely to result in a claim for PEC benefits, immediate written notice should be given to Hertz. Hertz will provide You with a claim form and the address of the insurance company which is providing the coverage.

> IF YOU RENT AN ELECTRIC VEHICLE (EV), THE FOLLOWING ELECTRIC VEHICLE RENTAL TERMS AND CONDITIONS APPLY IN ADDITION TO THE RENTAL TERMS AND CONDITIONS ABOVE.
> 
> These Electric Vehicle Rental Terms (“Rental Terms”) are between The Hertz Corporation and its affiliates (“Hertz” or “us”) and You and apply to a rental of an electric vehicle (“EV”) from Hertz. An EV is defined as a vehicle that exclusively uses battery power rather than gasoline or diesel fuel. These Electric Vehicle Rental Terms are in addition to the Terms and Conditions of the Rental Agreement applicable to your rental.
> 
> EV CHARGE LEVEL AT PICK-UP AND RETURN – Hertz will endeavor to provide the EV at time of vehicle pick-up with a battery charge of 80%, but that is not always the case. You are responsible to maintain a sufficient charge on the EV during your rental. You are never required to return a vehicle with more than 75% battery charge. If the EV is overdue Hertz may remotely disable and recover the EV. You will be responsible for the cost of any tow if the EV is not drivable due to a low battery or if it is overdue. You are not authorized to call a private tow on Hertz’ behalf. All tows of the EV must be by flatbed and must be arranged through Hertz Emergency Roadside Assistance.
> 
> RANGE – Range is the estimated distance an EV can travel on a single charge. The EV information provided with your reservation that describes a range is not guaranteed. The battery life of the EV is impacted by a number of factors including weather, driving and road conditions. It is your responsibility to ensure the EV has sufficient remaining battery life to return the EV to Hertz or reach an EV charging station.
> 
> CHARGING DURING RENTAL – Subject to Tesla’s terms and conditions and charging equipment standards, your EV may be able to access Tesla Superchargers to recharge. If You use a Tesla Supercharger to recharge the EV during your rental, that cost will be automatically billed back to Hertz and added to your rental charges with a 2.8% convenience fee. These charges may not appear on the final invoice and may be added later due to processing time. Battery charging limit on a Tesla should be set at 90% maximum. Hertz may recommend public charge point operators, who may provide Hertz incentives or rebates if you choose to charge at their locations, however, You may choose to charge the EV at any compatible public or private charging location at your own cost. You may also have to register and incur a fee at certain of these locations. You are responsible for any registration (including accepting terms and conditions and privacy policy) and any fees. If You do not move the EV promptly from the charging stall when it is finished charging You may incur an Idle fee for the time the EV remains in a charging stall after it is finished charging. You are responsible for and will indemnify Hertz for any Idle or similar fee incurred when the EV is on rent to You.  If the EV is overdue for return Hertz reserves the right to remotely disable the EV and remove the EV from the charging platform. If You rent a Tesla and are overdue to return, your access to the Tesla Superchargers will be removed.
> 
> ELECTRIC VEHICLE RECHARGING OPTIONS AND FEES - Renters may choose one of three electric vehicle recharging options: (1) Electric Vehicle Purchase Option (“EVPO”); (2) Electric Vehicle Service Charge (“EVSC”); or (3) you can recharge the vehicle yourself. You will not be charged EVSC if you return the vehicle within 5% of the battery level at pick up. You never have to return the vehicle with over 75% battery level.  The state of charge or battery level of the vehicle is described in Kilowatt-hours (kWh), a measure of electricity equivalent to 1 kilowatt (1,000 watts) of power expended for 1 hour. You will not receive a credit or refund for unused or excess charge left in the vehicle at return.
> 
> EVPO - Electric Vehicle Charge Purchase Option means you may purchase the state of charge in the battery at the time of pick up and can return the vehicle at any level.  The quoted price at the time of reservation is based on 80% of the average battery capacity for the EVs in the car class you reserved. The actual price may be lower or higher based on then-current EVPO fees at your rental location, the vehicle rented, and the battery level at the time of pick up. To calculate this fee, Hertz multiplies the kWh battery level at the time of pick up, times the per kWh rate shown on the Rental Record, which is based on average energy rates in the rental location state/province and a convenience fee combined.  You will not receive a credit or refund for the unused charge left in the battery at the time of return. If you choose the EVPO option and do not want it when you pick the vehicle up, you must ask for it to be taken off before leaving the facility.
> EVPO is optional. If not selected, you can return the vehicle within 5% the battery level at pick up to avoid the EV Service Charge (EVSC). If not selected and you do not adequately recharge, you will be charged based on the applicable EVSC required to recharge the vehicle to the same battery level as when you rented it.
> 
> As a cost-savings benefit to You, if You drive less than 75 miles, you will be charged the lesser of the EVPO and the EVSC rate.
> 
> EVSC - The Electric Vehicle Service Charge will apply if you do not purchase EVPO and you do not return your vehicle within 5% of the battery level at pick up. To calculate this fee, Hertz multiplies the difference between the battery level at pick up and the battery level at return in kWhs, times the per kWh rate shown on the Rental Record, which is based on average energy rates in the rental location state/province and service fee combined. This rate will always be higher than our EVPO kWh rate. You will not receive a credit or refund if the battery level at return exceeds the battery level at pick up.
> You can avoid this charge by adequately recharging the vehicle prior to return as described below.
> 
> Recharge the Vehicle Yourself – If you do not purchase EVPO, you will not be charged EVSC so long as you return the vehicle within 5% of the battery level at pick up. If you receive a vehicle with 80% battery or greater, you are only required to return the vehicle with 75% battery.
> THE COST PER KILOWATT OF THE EV PURCHASE OPTION WILL ALWAYS BE LOWER THAN THE EV SERVICE CHARGE COST PER KILOWATT. BUT IF YOU ELECT THE EV PURCHASE OPTION YOU WILL NOT RECEIVE A REFUND OR CREDIT FOR CHARGE LEFT IN THE BATTERY AT THE TIME OF RETURN. THE COST OF RECHARGING THE EV YOURSELF AT A LOCAL CHARGING STATION WILL GENERALLY BE LOWER THAN THE EV SERVICE CHARGE OR THE EV PURCHASE OPTION. HOWEVER, THE EV SERVICE CHARGE AND THE EV PURCHASE OPTION ALLOW FOR THE CONVENIENCE OF NOT HAVING TO STOP AND RECHARGE THE CAR PRIOR TO RETURN.
> 
> IN CERTAIN INSTANCES, EXCEPT WHERE PROHIBITED BY LAW, HERTZ EMPLOYS THE USE OF IN-VEHICLE TECHNOLOGIES AND TELEMATICS DEVICES, INCLUDING GLOBAL POSITIONING TECHNOLOGY, TO CALCULATE THE AMOUNT OF BATTERY USED IF YOU DO NOT PURCHASE EVPO AT THE BEGINNING OF YOUR RENTAL AND CHOOSE TO RETURN THE CAR WITH LESS CHARGE IN THE BATTERY THAN BEFORE YOU LEFT THE LOT. THE USE OF THESE IN-VEHICLE TECHNOLOGIES AND TELEMATICS DEVICES, INCLUDING GLOBAL POSITIONING TECHNOLOGY, IS NOT INTENDED TO BE AN ACCURATE MEASUREMENT OF THE AMOUNT OF CHARGE IN THE BATTERY, BUT INSTEAD, IS A CONFIRMATION FOR THE PRIOR VISUAL ESTIMATE CONDUCTED BY MANUAL READ. ANY AMOUNT OF BATTERY CHARGED IS LIMITED SOLELY TO THE ESTIMATE PROVIDED BY THESE DEVICES, REGARDLESS OF THE AMOUNT OF CHARGE IN THE BATTERY. YOU MAY ELECT FOR A “VISUAL CONFIRMATION” OF THE TELEMATICS ESTIMATE UPON RETURN OF THE CAR. FURTHER, YOU MAY ALWAYS OPT OUT OF THIS OPTION ALTOGETHER BY PURCHASING EVPO AT THE BEGINNING OF THE RENTAL.
> 
> DAMAGE TO CHARGING STATIONS – You are responsible for any damage to the EV, the charging station equipment or the charging location when charging the EV during your rental.  You will indemnify Hertz for any charges, fines, or penalties You incur for any damage or loss to the EV, the charging station or location during your rental.
> 
> EQUIPMENT – The EV will be provided to You with certain equipment for which You are responsible. You are responsible to notify Hertz if any of the following equipment is not with the EV at the time of pick up. Otherwise, You will be charged for any missing equipment at return. Loss Damage Waiver (LDW) does not apply to damage or loss of the equipment provided with the EV.
> 
> Key card or fob – You are responsible to return the Key card or Key fob upon your rental return. If the Key card or fob is damaged or lost, You will be charged to replace the Key Card or fob and a service fee. The Key card or Key fob must only be used to charge the EV You have rented. Sharing the Key card or Key fob, using additional Key cards or Key fobs to charge the EV, or charging other vehicles is prohibited. Any misuse of the Key card or Key fob in breach of these Rental Terms will result in additional usage charges.
> 
> Tesla Charging Kit – The Tesla Charging Kit consists of 1 Mobile Connector; 1 Storage Bag; and 1 NEMA 5-15 Adapter. You are responsible to return all contents of the Charging Kit upon your rental return.  If the Charging Kit, or any part of the contents are damaged or lost, You will be charged for a complete Charging Kit, as these items are not available to be replaced individually, and a service fee.
> 
> J1772 Adapter – You are responsible to return the J1772 Adapter on your rental return. If this Adapter is damaged or lost, You will be charged to replace the Adapter and a service fee.
> 
> SOFTWARE UPDATES – The EV may contain onboard computers which periodically suggest software updates. You are not authorized to update the in-vehicle software at any time unless specifically requested to do so by a Hertz representative. If a software update prompt is received during your rental, please ignore this or press cancel. If You do update the software (other than following the explicit instruction of a Hertz representative) this is at your own risk and Hertz accepts no responsibility or liability whatsoever including, but not limited to, any loss of use, interruption of service, incompatibility with training materials or otherwise.

### Assistant
> Yep. This rental jacket helps you. **A lot.** The agent saying “mandatory for Lyft drivers” is not matching the documents unless they can produce a **separate Lyft/Hertz rate rule** that says that.
> 
> ## The useful clauses
> 
> ### 1. LDW is repeatedly described as optional
> 
> The jacket says:
> 
> > “The purchase of this Loss Damage Waiver product is not mandatory and may be declined.”
> 
> Then Section 4 says:
> 
> > “The following products are optional…”  
> > “Purchase of optional Loss Damage Waiver…”  
> > “Purchase of Limited Loss Damage Waiver…”  
> > “Damage waivers entail an additional charge… but are optional and may be declined.”
> 
> So if Hertz says LDW/LLDW is mandatory for Lyft rentals, the response is:
> 
> > “Please identify the Lyft-specific document that overrides this and says separate LDW/LLDW charges are mandatory.”
> 
> Because the master terms do **not** say that.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. Premium Roadside is also optional
> 
> This is big.
> 
> The jacket says:
> 
> > “Basic Emergency Roadside Service is included with every rental…”
> 
> Then:
> 
> > “PERS is an optional service…”
> 
> So Premium Roadside is not mandatory either, based on the jacket.
> 
> That directly supports your claim:
> 
> > I was charged Premium Roadside even though basic roadside was already included, and the premium version is described as optional.
> 
> Also, if they charged you Premium Roadside and it failed when you needed lockout/battery help, that’s even worse for them.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 3. Section 7 only says LDW/PERS are payable “if applicable”
> 
> Section 7(d) says:
> 
> > “LDW, PERS, PAI/PEC and LIS charges, **if applicable**, are due and payable…”
> 
> That does **not** mean mandatory. It means if the product applies to the rental record, the charge accrues daily.
> 
> So the issue is still:
> 
> > Who made it applicable, when, and where did I authorize that?
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 4. The Lyft Addendum still matters most
> 
> The Lyft addendum says if there is a conflict, the Lyft addendum controls.
> 
> And that addendum says:
> 
> > LDW “will be included” with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms.
> 
> So the clean distinction is:
> 
> ## Included LDW protection ≠ separate optional LDW daily add-on
> 
> They are trying to blur that. Don’t let them.
> 
> Say:
> 
> > “If the Lyft program includes LDW subject to a deductible, that is different from charging me a separate optional LDW/LLDW daily product.”
> 
> That’s the whole fight.
> 
> ---
> 
> # The contradiction stack
> 
> Use this logic:
> 
> | Hertz/Lyft claim | Document problem |
> |---|---|
> | “LDW is mandatory for Lyft drivers” | Master terms say LDW/LLDW is optional and may be declined. |
> | “Premium Roadside is mandatory” | Jacket says basic roadside is included and PERS is optional. |
> | “It was always required” | First week had no LDW/LLDW charge. |
> | “You accepted it” | Receipt says charges were “added during rental,” so they need proof of when/how you accepted it. |
> | “It can’t be removed” | Hertz sent a corrected rental agreement one minute later removing LDW and Premium Roadside. |
> | “It is still on the record” | Then Hertz’s system conflicts with Hertz’s corrected agreement. |
> 
> That is not you being confused. Their records are inconsistent.
> 
> ---
> 
> # Say this to Hertz now
> 
> :::writing{variant="standard" id="64219"}
> I need this escalated because the documents do not support what I’m being told.
> 
> The Hertz Master Terms say Loss Damage Waiver is optional, may be declined, and is offered for an additional charge. Section 4 also describes LDW, PDW, and LLDW as optional damage waiver products. The same terms say Basic Emergency Roadside Service is included with every rental and that Premium Emergency Roadside Assistance is optional.
> 
> So if Hertz is saying separate LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges are mandatory for Lyft drivers, I need the specific Lyft/Hertz document or rate rule that says that and overrides the Master Terms.
> 
> The Lyft Driver Rental Program Addendum says LDW will be included with the rental, subject to the $1,000 deductible and program terms. Included LDW protection is not the same thing as a separate optional daily LDW/LLDW product added during the rental.
> 
> My first week had no LDW/LLDW charge. Hertz’s closed receipt says LDW and Premium Road Service were “charges added during rental.” Hertz also sent a corrected renewal agreement removing LDW and Premium Roadside. So I need Hertz to identify the controlling agreement and explain, in writing, why the system still shows these charges.
> :::
> 
> ---
> 
> ## The exact question to pin them down
> 
> Ask this:
> 
> > “Are you saying LDW/LLDW is mandatory as **included program protection**, or mandatory as a **separate daily paid add-on**?”
> 
> Then:
> 
> > “Where does the contract say that separate daily paid add-on is mandatory for Lyft?”
> 
> If they cannot answer, ask for escalation.
> 
> ## One more important clause
> 
> Section 15 says rental reps are not authorized to waive or change terms except by signed writing from an authorized Hertz representative.
> 
> So if a local agent added LDW/PERS during the rental, your question becomes:
> 
> > “Where is the written authorization or rental record showing I approved that change?”
> 
> Not vibes. Not “the system does it.” Written authorization.
> 
> ## Bottom line
> 
> This jacket makes your argument stronger:
> 
> - **LDW/LLDW = optional in master terms**
> - **Premium Roadside = optional**
> - **Basic roadside = included**
> - **Lyft addendum says LDW included**
> - **Receipt says add-ons were added during rental**
> - **Corrected agreement removed them**
> 
> So the answer to “what’s the real agreement?” is:
> 
> > Hertz needs to identify the controlling Lyft-specific agreement, because the documents they gave you are internally inconsistent. Until they do, you dispute the separate added LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges.

> 
> ## Two important fixes jump out immediately
> 
> ### 1. The generated `index.html` has a build bug
> 
> Your `build.py` is inserting Python lists directly into the HTML:
> 
> ```html
> ['<button class="nav-item"...']
> ```
> 
> That means the site will visually show brackets/quotes instead of clean sidebar/content HTML.
> 
> **Fix in `build.py`:**
> 
> Replace:
> 
> ```python
> {sidebar_html}
> ```
> 
> with:
> 
> ```python
> {''.join(sidebar_html)}
> ```
> 
> And replace:
> 
> ```python
> {sections_html}
> ```
> 
> with:
> 
> ```python
> {''.join(sections_html)}
> ```
> 
> That is why the dashboard looks broken. Easy fix.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### 2. Remove the word “nuke” from formal letters
> 
> In both Hertz/Lyft formal demand letters, the draft says:
> 
> > “Issue a refund/credit … to nuke the disputed add-on charges…”
> 
> That needs to be:
> 
> > “Issue a refund/credit … to remove and reverse the disputed add-on charges…”
> 
> “Nuke” is fine when we’re talking, not in a certified/legal-style packet.

> ## Timeline Correction / Expanded Operational Failure Chain
> 
> ### June 1, 2026 — Registration/Sticker Compliance Issue Begins
> Lyft/Hertz instructed Cody to appear at the Indianapolis Hertz/Lyft location because the vehicle required a registration/sticker document update. Cody treated this as a compliance and safety issue because the vehicle appeared to have a plate/sticker problem that could affect lawful operation.
> 
> ### June 1–2, 2026 — Compliance Trip and Appointment Failure
> Cody traveled to Indianapolis to comply with the registration/sticker instruction. While attempting to resolve the issue, the appointment/swap process was canceled or blocked due to an outstanding balance on the account. That balance was affected by disputed LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges that Hertz later described as added during the rental.
> 
> ### June 2–6, 2026 — No Sticker, No Swap, No Reliable Resolution
> Cody remained in Indianapolis attempting to resolve the registration/sticker and vehicle-swap problem. The branch did not have the sticker ready and did not provide a replacement vehicle. Cody was repeatedly told to come back later or the next day. During this period, Cody did not use the vehicle for at least two days because he reasonably believed the plate/sticker issue made operation unsafe, noncompliant, or risky.
> 
> ### June 6–9, 2026 — Disputed Balance Continues Blocking Resolution
> The unresolved balance and renewal/account status continued to interfere with the ability to swap the vehicle or complete the vehicle update. Cody remained dependent on the same vehicle despite the unresolved compliance issue because Lyft/Hertz had not provided a corrected vehicle, had not completed the sticker update, and had not removed the vehicle from service.
> 
> ### June 9–10, 2026 — Bank Fees and Account Pressure
> Repeated collection attempts and disputed balances caused additional account pressure, return-car warnings, and overdraft/NSF fees. This further delayed resolution and created a cycle where the disputed charges themselves prevented Cody from accessing the swap or correction needed to fix the underlying vehicle problem.
> 
> ### June 11, 2026 — Key Fob / Lockout Failure
> The vehicle became unusable again due to key fob/battery failure, causing Cody to be locked out and unable to work. Roadside assistance was ineffective because the rental record information needed for assistance was inside the locked vehicle and support could not locate the rental without it. Cody paid out of pocket for a replacement key fob battery and related transportation.
> 
> ### June 12, 2026 — Sticker Finally Provided, But No Vehicle Swap
> The registration/sticker issue was finally resolved around Friday, June 12. However, Hertz still did not complete the requested vehicle swap despite the prior battery/key fob issue and the extended period of failed resolution. Cody returned home with the same unreliable vehicle.
> 
> ### June 15, 2026 — Repeat Battery Failure
> After the earlier key fob/battery issue and after Hertz had been notified, the vehicle battery failed again. Cody had to keep the vehicle running after jump/start assistance because he feared it would not restart, causing additional fuel loss, downtime, and safety risk.
> 
> ### Timeline Significance
> This sequence shows that Cody’s losses were not caused by voluntary delay. They were caused by a Hertz/Lyft operational loop: a required compliance visit, unresolved sticker/tag issue, disputed balances, canceled or blocked appointments, unavailable swaps, ineffective roadside support, and repeated vehicle failure.
> :::

### Assistant
> Yes. **That’s the real story.** And you’re right: we need to stop making it sound like a confusing contract puzzle. It’s simpler and uglier than that.
> 
> The current packet already has the evidence structure and $604.01 minimum demand, but this fuller chain needs to be added because it explains *why* the harm snowballed. The existing extracted matter file has the summary, timeline, strategy, and claim math, but the daily sticker/swap/balance trap is still underdeveloped. fileciteturn2file0
> 
> ## Lock this in as the core theory
> 
> They did **all** of this:
> 
> 1. **Advertised / represented the protections as included or optional.**
> 2. **Did not charge them at first.**
> 3. **Added them later after you left without clear authorization.**
> 4. **Used those added charges to create balances.**
> 5. **Used those balances to block swaps / appointments.**
> 6. **Gave you a car with plates/sticker expiring before the rental period they sold you.**
> 7. **Told you to drive to Indy to fix it, then didn’t have the sticker.**
> 8. **Couldn’t be reached by you or even by corporate.**
> 9. **Strung you along day after day: no sticker, no clean car, no swap.**
> 10. **Finally gave the sticker but still refused/failed to swap the bad vehicle.**
> 11. **Left you with a car that had key fob failure and battery failure.**
> 12. **Caused lost work time, bank fees, food insecurity, hotel/fuel costs, physical danger, job loss, and caregiving disruption.**
> 
> That is not “customer inconvenience.” That is a **billing-and-service failure chain**.
> 
> ## Stronger framing
> 
> Do **not** say “fraud” first in the main packet. Say:
> 
> > unauthorized, undisclosed, inconsistent with written representations, deceptive, unfair, and financially harmful.
> 
> Save “fraudulent” for escalation if they deny the obvious or if a regulator asks you to describe intent.
> 
> ## Revised plain-English case paragraph
> 
> :::writing{variant="document" id="28391"}
> Hertz and Lyft represented the Express Drive protections as included in the rental program or optional. These charges were not present at the beginning of my rental and later appeared after I had already left the facility, without my knowledge, approval, or authorization. Hertz then treated those same charges as mandatory, even though the rental jacket and program materials describe them as included or optional.
> 
> Those unauthorized add-on charges created balances that blocked my ability to swap or resolve the vehicle. At the same time, Hertz had rented me a vehicle with plates/sticker status expiring before the rental period I was sold. I was instructed to drive to Indianapolis to fix the registration/sticker issue, but the branch did not have the sticker ready and could not provide a swap. I was repeatedly told to come back, while the branch was unreachable by phone and even corporate support could not reliably reach them.
> 
> This caused a rolling operational failure: I lost work time, spent money on fuel, food, lodging, and basic supplies, and was left with no practical way to get home while still being charged. I reasonably refrained from driving the vehicle at times because of the plate/sticker issue, and when I later resumed driving, it was because Hertz/Lyft left me with no replacement and no income alternative.
> 
> The vehicle also had key fob and battery failures. I was locked out, roadside assistance was ineffective, and I had to pay out of pocket for a key fob battery and transportation. The battery failed again afterward while I was at the hospital assisting my mother, causing more lost peak-time work. These failures caused direct financial harm, bank fees, job loss, caregiving disruption, food insecurity, and physical safety risk.
> :::
> 
> ## This is the money line
> 
> > **The charges were not there, then they appeared. The vehicle was not compliant, then they failed to fix it. The balance they created blocked the swap I needed. Then the defective vehicle failed again. Refund my money and credit the unusable time.**
> 
> That’s the case.
>

> 
> - **Pickup problem:** could not even reliably confirm pickup / support access.
> - **Initial rental:** vehicle issued with plates/sticker expiring before the expected rental period.
> - **Week 1:** no LDW/PERS charges.
> - **Week 2/3:** LDW/PERS appeared without authorization.
> - **Compliance trip:** told to bring car to Indy for sticker issue.
> - **Branch failure:** no sticker ready after you arrived.
> - **Corporate failure:** corporate said contact front desk, but front desk did not answer; corporate also could not get through.
> - **Swap blocked #1:** outstanding balance blocked swap.
> - **Balance cause discovered later:** balance inflated by added LDW/PERS and taxes.
> - **Swap blocked #2:** after you worked/borrowed money to clear balances, they still had no clean car and no sticker.
> - **Daily failure loop:** come back tomorrow; still no sticker, still no car.
> - **Friday:** sticker finally provided; swap still not completed.
> - **Return home:** came back with same unreliable vehicle.
> - **Lockout:** bad key fob battery / ineffective roadside.
> - **Repeat failure:** battery died again at hospital, causing peak-time income loss.
>

>

> 
> > **Stranded-driver mitigation, unusable-vehicle credit, and lost earning time caused by Hertz/Lyft’s billing and vehicle-compliance failures.**
>

> 
> - days you did not drive because of plate/sticker fear,

> - food and basic supplies while stranded.
>

### User
> ok using the {{}} does not populate anything

### Assistant
> Yep. My mistake. `{{ }}` does **nothing** unless a template engine like Jinja is actually rendering it.
> 
> For Zoottel, use **markers** that your script replaces, or have the script generate the real text directly.
> 
> Use this instead:
> 
> :::writing{variant="document" id="32784"}
> ---
> type: folder_index
> status: active
> ai_ingest: true
> shareable: conditional
> ---
> 
> # Folder Index
> 
> ## Purpose
> 
> <!-- ZOOTTEL:PURPOSE -->
> 
> ## Contents
> 
> <!-- ZOOTTEL:CONTENTS_TABLE -->
> 
> ## Key Files
> 
> <!-- ZOOTTEL:KEY_FILES -->
> 
> ## Open Items
> 
> <!-- ZOOTTEL:OPEN_ITEMS -->
> 
> ## Notes
> 
> <!-- ZOOTTEL:NOTES -->
> :::
> 
> Tell Codex/IDE this:
> 
> > Do not leave template placeholders like `{{folder_name}}` in `_index.md` files. For each folder, generate the actual `_index.md` using the folder name, path, and scanned contents. Replace the `ZOOTTEL:` marker sections with real generated content.
> 
> So the final `_index.md` should say:
> 
> ```md
> # 20_evidence
> 
> ## Purpose
> 
> Stores source evidence files for the Hertz/Lyft rental dispute.
> 
> ## Contents
> 
> | File | Type | Updated | Notes |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | 20260612_Hertz_Receipt_Closed_582293714_EV022.pdf | PDF | 2026-06-15 | Closed receipt showing added charges |
> ```
> 
> No curly braces. No fake variables. Actual generated content.

### Assistant
> Got you. This is the **clean professional version of “run me my money”** — no escape-hatch wording, no helping them reconcile their mess. I based it on the current matter packet structure and the evidence map already in your QiNexus extraction. fileciteturn2file0
> 
> :::writing{variant="document" id="84172"}
> # FORMAL NOTICE OF DISPUTE, DEMAND FOR REFUND, AND REQUEST FOR ACCOUNT CORRECTION
> 
> **Date:** June 15, 2026
> 
> **From:**  
> Cody Rice-Velasquez  
> Lyft Express Drive Driver / Hertz Renter  
> Email: crice4485@gmail.com  
> 
> **To:**  
> The Hertz Corporation  
> Hertz Executive Customer Relations / Billing Disputes  
> 
> **And To:**  
> Lyft, Inc.  
> Express Drive Support / Driver Billing / Corporate Escalations  
> 
> **Subject:** Formal Dispute and Demand for Refund — Hertz/Lyft Express Drive Rental Records 582293714 and 594402524
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. Rental Records and Vehicle
> 
> This notice concerns the following Hertz/Lyft Express Drive rental records:
> 
> | Item | Details |
> |---|---|
> | Closed Hertz Rental Record | 582293714 |
> | Active / Renewal Hertz Rental Record | 594402524 |
> | Vehicle | 2024 Nissan Sentra |
> | License Plate | TN 757BMYJ |
> | Program | Lyft Express Drive / Hertz Driver Rental Program |
> | Location | Indianapolis Hertz / Lyft Express Drive location |
> 
> This is a formal billing dispute and demand for immediate refund, account correction, and reimbursement for direct financial harm caused by Hertz and Lyft’s billing and vehicle-service failures.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 2. Executive Summary
> 
> Hertz and Lyft represented the Express Drive rental protections as included in the rental program or optional. Hertz’s own rental terms describe Loss Damage Waiver / Limited Loss Damage Waiver and Premium Emergency Roadside Assistance as optional products. Lyft and Hertz program materials also represent required rental protection and roadside support as included in the Express Drive program.
> 
> Despite that, LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges appeared after I left the rental facility. They were not on the first week’s rental billing. I did not add them, approve them, request them, or authorize them. Hertz’s own closed receipt later labeled those items as “Charges Added During Rental.”
> 
> Those unauthorized and disputed charges created balances that blocked my ability to swap or correct the vehicle. At the same time, Hertz had issued me a vehicle with plate/sticker status expiring before the rental period I was sold. Hertz/Lyft then required me to travel to Indianapolis for a registration/sticker issue, but the branch did not have the sticker ready, could not provide a clean replacement vehicle, and was repeatedly unreachable by phone. Even Hertz corporate support could not reliably reach the branch.
> 
> The result was not a minor inconvenience. The result was a rolling failure chain: unauthorized charges, blocked swaps, unresolved registration/sticker issues, days of lost use, repeated trips to the branch, out-of-pocket costs, bank fees, inability to get home, food insecurity, unsafe heat exposure, ineffective roadside support, lockout, key fob failure, battery failure, lost earning time, loss of caregiver employment, and disruption to my mother’s care.
> 
> I am requesting immediate refund and credit. Hertz and Lyft need to correct the account and return the money deducted or charged because of these improper add-ons and the resulting service failures.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 3. Core Billing Dispute: Charges Were Included or Optional, Then Added Anyway
> 
> The billing issue is direct.
> 
> Hertz/Lyft represented LDW/LLDW and roadside protections as included in the Express Drive rental program or optional. The charges were not present at the beginning of my rental. They later appeared without my knowledge or authorization.
> 
> Hertz and Lyft do not get to advertise or document these items as included or optional, fail to charge them at first, add them later without authorization, and then say the same charges are mandatory separate daily charges.
> 
> That is the basis of this dispute.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 4. What Happened
> 
> ### A. Pickup and Initial Rental Problems
> 
> At the beginning of this rental relationship, I could not even reliably confirm basic pickup and support details. I was issued a vehicle that had plate/sticker status expiring within a short period, even though I was entering the Express Drive program and expected to have the vehicle for a longer rental period.
> 
> This created the first vehicle-compliance problem before I had even had a fair chance to operate the rental normally.
> 
> ### B. Charges Were Not There, Then Appeared Later
> 
> During the first rental week, LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges were not charged as separate add-ons.
> 
> Later, those charges appeared. I did not authorize them. I did not request them. I did not approve them at the counter, in the app, by phone, or by any later agreement.
> 
> For closed Rental Record 582293714, Hertz’s final receipt listed:
> 
> | Disputed Item | Amount |
> |---|---:|
> | LDW / Loss Damage Waiver | $263.76 |
> | Premium Road Service | $24.24 |
> | Estimated related tax at 17% | $48.96 |
> | Closed receipt disputed total | $336.96 |
> 
> Those charges appeared under the category “Charges Added During Rental.” That is exactly the problem: they were added after the rental began, without my authorization.
> 
> ### C. The Charges Created Balances That Blocked Vehicle Resolution
> 
> The added LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges created or contributed to balances that should not have existed. Those balances then blocked the vehicle swap and resolution process.
> 
> When I attempted to swap or correct the vehicle, I was told there was an outstanding balance. I later discovered that the balance problem was tied to the added protection charges and related taxes.
> 
> This happened more than once. The disputed balance blocked my ability to swap the vehicle and delayed the resolution of the plate/sticker issue. Hertz/Lyft created the billing problem and then used that same billing problem to deny or delay the service needed to fix the vehicle.
> 
> ### D. Registration / Sticker Failure and Indianapolis Branch Problems
> 
> Hertz/Lyft instructed me to bring the vehicle to Indianapolis for a registration/sticker issue. I spent my gas, time, and lost work opportunity traveling to the branch because Hertz/Lyft told me the vehicle needed to be corrected.
> 
> When I arrived, the branch did not have the sticker ready.
> 
> I was told to come back later or the next day. I stayed in Indianapolis because I was trying to comply and resolve the issue. The next day, the sticker still was not available. The branch still did not provide a clean swap vehicle.
> 
> This continued day after day.
> 
> Corporate support repeatedly told me I had to contact or work through the branch, but the branch was not answering. Corporate support also could not reliably reach the branch. It is unreasonable for Hertz/Lyft to require a customer to resolve a vehicle-compliance issue through a branch that the customer and corporate support cannot reach.
> 
> ### E. Swap Was Blocked Again Even After I Tried to Clear the Balance
> 
> Because of the disputed charges and balances, I had to push hard to get money together, including help from friends and family, just to pay balances that should not have been charged in the first place.
> 
> After I finally got the past-due balances paid, I returned again expecting the sticker issue or swap to be resolved. I was then told the sticker still was not there, and the branch did not have clean cars available to swap.
> 
> This was not a real solution. I was not offered a reliable same-day alternative, a dirty-car swap option, a clear appointment time, a supervisor resolution, or a guaranteed correction. I was effectively told there was nothing they could do.
> 
> I returned again on later days. Still no sticker. Still no vehicle swap. Still no reliable resolution.
> 
> Finally, the sticker was available, but Hertz still did not complete the requested vehicle swap. I returned home with the same unreliable vehicle.
> 
> ### F. Vehicle Non-Use and Unsafe Forced Use
> 
> I lost use of the vehicle multiple times.
> 
> At minimum, I did not drive for at least two days because I reasonably believed the registration/sticker issue made the vehicle unsafe, risky, or potentially noncompliant to operate. Once I realized Lyft had not deactivated the vehicle and I had no practical alternative, I resumed driving because I had no other way to earn income.
> 
> That does not make the situation acceptable. Hertz/Lyft left me with a vehicle that had an unresolved compliance issue and no replacement, then continued charging me while I was forced to choose between not earning money and driving a vehicle I reasonably believed had unresolved documentation issues.
> 
> ### G. Lockout, Key Fob Failure, Roadside Failure, and Battery Failure
> 
> The vehicle also had key fob and battery problems.
> 
> I was locked out because the key fob battery failed. Roadside assistance was ineffective. I was told support needed information that was inside the locked vehicle, and the rental could not be located without that information. I had to pay out of pocket for a replacement key fob battery and related transportation.
> 
> Those costs were:
> 
> | Item | Amount |
> |---|---:|
> | Key fob battery | $18.18 |
> | Lyft transportation related to battery replacement | $6.59 |
> | Direct out-of-pocket subtotal | $24.77 |
> 
> The problems did not stop there. The vehicle battery failed again after Hertz had already been told there were vehicle/key/battery issues. The vehicle died while I was at the hospital dropping off items for my mother, causing additional lost time during peak earning hours and creating another safety and reliability problem.
> 
> This vehicle should have been swapped or repaired. Hertz/Lyft failed to do that.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 5. Direct Financial Harm
>

> | Corrected agreement difference, Record 594402524 | $98.28 |

>

>

> 
> | Category | Amount |
> |---|---:|
> | Section A — Disputed billing | $435.24 |
> | Section B — Out-of-pocket costs | $24.77 |
> | Section C — Confirmed bank fees | $144.00 |
> | Confirmed minimum reimbursement demand | $604.01 |
> 
> This $604.01 is the confirmed minimum. It does not include all stranded-driver expenses, lost earning time, food, lodging, fuel, basic supplies, additional bank impact, caregiver job loss, or vehicle downtime credit.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 6. Additional Damages and Pending Amounts
> 
> I am also requesting review, credit, and reimbursement for the following categories:
> 
> 1. Lost earning time caused by the plate/sticker issue, repeated branch visits, blocked swaps, lockout, and battery failure.
> 2. Rental credit for days and partial days when the vehicle was unusable, unsafe, or reasonably not drivable because Hertz/Lyft had not resolved the registration/sticker or vehicle reliability issues.
> 3. Fuel and travel costs for repeated trips to the Indianapolis branch.
> 4. Food and basic living expenses while stranded in Indianapolis.
> 5. Hotel/lodging expenses or other costs incurred because I could not reasonably return home while the vehicle issue remained unresolved.
> 6. Basic clothing and hygiene supplies purchased because I was unexpectedly stuck away from home.
> 7. Additional bank fees and financial losses pending review.
> 8. Lost caregiver employment and related financial impact.
> 9. Safety-related harm caused by lockout, heat exposure, inability to access help, and being left with a defective vehicle.
> 
> These damages were not optional spending. They were mitigation costs and consequences caused by Hertz/Lyft’s billing, communication, branch-service, and vehicle-maintenance failures.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 7. Why Hertz and Lyft Are Both Responsible
> 
> Hertz supplied and controlled the vehicle, rental agreement, branch service, repair/swap process, registration/sticker correction, roadside process, and rental records.
> 
> Lyft administered the Express Drive driver-facing program, app messaging, driver earnings deductions, account restrictions, and support process.
> 
> The harm happened through the joint Express Drive program. Hertz and Lyft should not shift responsibility back and forth while I am charged, blocked, stranded, and left without a reliable vehicle.
> 
> Hertz and Lyft must coordinate the refund, credit, and account correction directly.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 8. Required Action
> 
> I demand that Hertz and Lyft take the following actions:
> 
> 1. Refund or credit the confirmed minimum amount of $604.01 immediately.
> 2. Remove and reverse all unauthorized LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside charges and related taxes.
> 3. Confirm that no further LDW/LLDW or Premium Roadside charges will be deducted unless there is clear signed or digital authorization from me.
> 4. Credit rental time for days and hours when the vehicle was unusable, unsafe, or reasonably not drivable due to Hertz/Lyft’s registration/sticker, branch, lockout, key fob, battery, or swap failures.
> 5. Reimburse documented mitigation costs, including fuel, lodging, food, supplies, and travel connected to the Indianapolis sticker/swap failure.
> 6. Reimburse confirmed bank fees and review additional pending bank impacts.
> 7. Provide a complete itemized ledger showing all charges, deductions, reversals, holds, taxes, payments, credits, and adjustments from May 19, 2026 to the present.
> 8. Provide all records showing when LDW/LLDW and Premium Roadside were added, by whom, by what method, and under what authorization.
> 9. Preserve all call recordings, branch notes, account notes, internal messages, app messages, rental records, inspection records, roadside records, vehicle maintenance records, and billing records related to Rental Records 582293714 and 594402524.
> 10. Provide a written response within ten business days.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 9. Preservation Notice
> 
> Hertz and Lyft are instructed to preserve all documents, records, audio recordings, internal notes, app logs, payment logs, branch communications, support tickets, roadside records, vehicle maintenance records, and rental/billing history related to this dispute.
> 
> This includes records from Hertz corporate support, the Indianapolis branch, Lyft Express Drive support, driver billing systems, roadside assistance systems, and any third-party support vendors involved.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 10. Closing Statement
> 
> This situation was not caused by my delay or refusal to cooperate. I repeatedly tried to comply, contact the branch, resolve the sticker issue, clear balances, swap the vehicle, and keep working.
> 
> The problem is that Hertz and Lyft represented the protections as included or optional, added charges after the rental began without my authorization, used those disputed charges to create balances that blocked the swap and resolution process, failed to provide the sticker when I was told to come in, failed to provide a replacement vehicle, failed to provide effective roadside support, and left me with a vehicle that continued to fail.
> 
> I am requesting immediate refund, credit, and account correction.
> 
> Sincerely,
> 
> Cody Rice-Velasquez  
> Lyft Express Drive Driver / Hertz Renter
